**Pitfalls.** ["HARD RULE — raw Bronze immutability: the new reader only READS via `lander.s3.open(..., 'rb')`; never write/mutate Bronze objects, and do not change RawLander landing semantics beyond ADDING the World Bank ingest call.", "HARD RULE — deterministic numeric merge, no LLM on numbers: World Bank parsing must stay pure pandas inside `load_worldbank_frame`/`read_worldbank_json` (load.py:39-57, merge.py:77-89). Do not introduce any LLM or value rewriting; the crosswalk LLM is only for HU/DE labels and World Bank labels are English (map by rule).", "Read World Bank as BYTES, not text: `load_worldbank_frame` expects raw bytes (it does `json.loads(raw)`), and routing through `_read_text` (pipeline.py:277-281) would pull in the cp1251/encoding bug that is GAP-014's scope. Add a dedicated `_read_bytes` helper instead.", "Glob/path-prefix correctness: in s3 mode `_list_bronze_files` globs `{BRONZE_BUCKET}/stats/<source>/*/ingest_date=*/*` (pipeline.py:259) where BRONZE_BUCKET defaults to `bronze`. The fake s3 in the test must key paths WITH the `bronze/` prefix and return POSIX-style strings (forward slashes) — `_is_data_file` normalizes backslashes but the glob match happens against whatever the fake returns. `_dataset_id_from_path(path, 'worldbank')` (pipeline.py:284-306) derives the dataset id from the segment AFTER `worldbank`, so seed paths like `bronze/stats/worldbank/IS.RRS.PASG.KM/ingest_date=2026-06-22/IS.RRS.PASG.KM.json`.", "Catalogue skip: live glob `stats/worldbank/*/...` will include any `_catalogue_*` dataset dir; the local `frames_from_bronze` skips `name.startswith('_')` (load.py:97). Mirror that skip in `_read_bronze_worldbank` or a catalogue JSON (not a `[meta, records]` time series) could log a spurious 'no time-series records' warning. `.meta.json` sidecars are already excluded by `_is_data_file` (pipeline.py:264-266) — keep the `include` lambda as `endswith('.json')` (it will also match `.meta.json` names, but `_is_data_file` filters those out).", "Eurostat dtype drift (note, not a required change): the live Eurostat reader (pipeline.py:204-209 via `_read_tsv`) reads with pandas default dtypes while local `load_eurostat_frame` uses `dtype=str` (load.py:66). Outputs from any optional live run go under output/evidence/ only.", "Fake s3 `.open` must support both 'rb' (bytes) and 'r' (text) and behave as a context manager (the code uses `with lander.s3.open(...) as f`). For the stats test only 'rb' is needed, but model it on s3fs so it is reusable for GAP-020.", "Do not fabricate data: the WB fixture `IS.RRS.PASG.KM.json` contains a null-value row (2022) and real values for 2021 — `load_worldbank_frame` keeps nulls as-is and never invents rows; assert on presence of the frame/`source_system`, not on a hand-typed value count, to stay robust."]

### GAP-019 — Make the Bronze "automatic updates" scheduler deployable, restart-safe, and MinIO-fault-tolerant

`HIGH` · level **ops** · effort **M** · depends on: none (independent of GAP-005 wiring, GAP-013 live-MinIO, and GAP-009 Spark). Do NOT wait on GAP-005: this gap is about deployability + fault tolerance of the existing stats/news batches, not about adding KSH/UIC/StatAustria sources. If GAP-005 lands first, _run_batch must still degrade gracefully regardless of which ingest_fns are wired.

**Build:** Wrap each Bronze ingest batch so an unreachable MinIO degrades (logs + writes a run-evidence manifest) instead of crashing, make the schedule loop swallow per-batch failures, and add a deployable scheduler host (docker-compose service + documented systemd-timer/cron alternative) with a runbook line.

**Context.** "Automatic updates" of web-collected data is an explicit graded course requirement (docs/STATE_AND_ROADMAP.md: "Scheduler wiring (GAP-005) ... for the 'automatic updates' requirement"; docs/TASKS.md Contract C: "A scheduled run lands fresh Bronze (automatic-updates demo)"). The Bronze scheduler in src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/run.py is the only component that satisfies it, and it sits at the very front of the pipeline (web sources -> Bronze raw landing -> Silver -> Gold -> Spark -> report). Today that scheduler is a demo-grade in-process loop with no deployable host and no fault tolerance, so it cannot be honestly cited as "automatic updates" in the report. This is pure ops/orchestration: it must not change any Bronze write semantics, Silver/Gold logic, or numbers.

**Problem.** Three concrete defects, all in the Bronze scheduler and its lander:

1) MinIO-unreachable boot crashes with no handling. src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/run.py:54-58 ("schedule" mode) calls run_stats() then run_news() at boot. run_stats() (run.py:30) and run_news() (run.py:39) each construct RawLander() eagerly. RawLander.__init__ (src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/lander.py:47-54) builds s3fs.S3FileSystem(...) and immediately calls self.s3.exists(BRONZE_BUCKET) at lander.py:52 — a network round-trip to MinIO (S3_ENDPOINT default http://localhost:9000, bronze/config.py:13). If MinIO is down this raises a botocore/connection error that propagates up through run_stats/run_news into main() (run.py:55-56) completely unhandled, killing the whole scheduler process before any cadence is even registered.

2) Cadence is in-memory only, so it is not restart-safe. The only record of "when to run next" is the in-process `schedule` library job list registered at run.py:57-58 (schedule.every().sunday.at("02:00"); schedule.every(365).days...). The loop at run.py:60-62 (while True: schedule.run_pending(); time.sleep(60)) holds this purely in memory. A process/container/host restart loses all timing and re-fires the boot batch; there is no deployable host (no systemd timer, no cron, no compose service) that re-establishes cadence across restarts. docker-compose.yml defines only `minio` and `createbuckets` — no scheduler service.

3) A single failing batch kills the whole loop. Even after boot, any exception inside run_stats()/run_news() raised from inside the while-loop (run.py:61) is unhandled and terminates the scheduler, so one transient MinIO/network blip permanently stops "automatic updates" with no self-recovery.

Net effect: the scheduler is a non-deployable demo that cannot be cited as a real automatic-update mechanism. GAP_REGISTER.md:47 cites bronze/run.py:54-62 as the locus.

**Steps.**
1. Read the four anchor sites end to end first: src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/run.py (whole file, 1-69), src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/lander.py:44-93, scripts/minio_smoke.py:61-136 (the fail-soft + evidence-manifest idiom to mirror), and src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/live_check.py:147-182 (write_manifest reuse candidate).
2. In src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/run.py add a storage preflight helper `def _storage_reachable() -> tuple[bool, str | None]` that constructs an s3fs.S3FileSystem from bronze.config (S3_ENDPOINT/S3_KEY/S3_SECRET) and calls fs.exists(BRONZE_BUCKET) inside try/except, returning (True, None) on success and (False, str(exc)) on any exception. Do NOT change RawLander.__init__ (raw Bronze write contract stays immutable) — the preflight is a separate, read-only reachability probe.
3. Add `def _write_run_manifest(out_dir: Path, *, batch: str, status: str, started_at: str, finished_at: str, storage_reachable: bool, error: str | None, landed: list[dict]) -> Path` that writes output/evidence/scheduler/<batch>-<UTC-timestamp>.json (status in {"completed","degraded","failed"}). Reuse the JSON-write shape from scripts/minio_smoke.py (_write_json) and the manifest field style from live_check.write_manifest. Outputs MUST go under output/ (hard rule) — default the evidence dir to output/evidence/scheduler.
4. Refactor run_stats() and run_news() (run.py:28-42) into a single guarded batch runner `def _run_batch(name: str, ingest_fns: list, *, evidence_dir: Path) -> str`: capture started_at; call _storage_reachable(); if not reachable, log.warning a clear MinIO-down message, write a status="degraded" manifest (storage_reachable=false, the error string, empty landed list), and RETURN the status WITHOUT raising or constructing RawLander; if reachable, construct RawLander() once and call each ingest_fn(lander) inside try/except per source (mirror live_check.py:127-145), accumulating per-source success/failure into `landed`, then write status="completed" (or "degraded" if any source failed) manifest. Keep run_stats()/run_news() as thin wrappers that call _run_batch so existing callers and CODEMAP wording stay valid.
5. Harden the schedule loop (run.py:54-62): wrap the boot batches and the per-tick schedule.run_pending() body in try/except that logs the exception and continues the loop (never let one bad batch kill cadence). Make boot batches use the degraded-not-crash path from _run_batch so a MinIO-down boot logs+records evidence and the loop still starts and keeps retrying on the next tick.
6. Add a deployable host #1 — docker-compose: add a `scheduler` service to docker-compose.yml that builds/uses the project image, depends_on: [minio, createbuckets], command `python -m railway_lakehouse.bronze.run schedule`, restart: unless-stopped (mirror the minio service's restart policy), and mounts/uses the same S3_* env defaults already in compose. This gives restart-safe cadence: the host (Docker) re-launches the process on crash/reboot and the degraded-boot path means a not-yet-ready MinIO no longer crash-loops.
7. Add a deployable host #2 — native: create deploy/railway-bronze-stats.service + .timer and deploy/railway-bronze-news.service + .timer systemd units (OnCalendar=yearly for stats, weekly for news; Persistent=true so missed runs fire after downtime — this is the real restart-safe cadence) that run `python -m railway_lakehouse.bronze.run stats` / `news` one-shot. Also document the equivalent two crontab lines as the lowest-common-denominator alternative. Put these unit files under deploy/ (new dir) so they are committed artifacts, not just prose.
8. Write the runbook: create docs/OPERATIONS.md (link it from docs/INDEX.md) with a 'Bronze automatic updates' section giving (a) the docker-compose scheduler one-liner `docker compose up -d scheduler`, (b) the systemd timer install lines, (c) the cron alternative, and (d) the degradation contract (MinIO down => degraded manifest under output/evidence/scheduler/, no crash). Add one runbook line to README.md under the MinIO section. Update docs/VERIFICATION.md with the new unit-test command and an 'automatic-updates demo' manual check.
9. Add a deterministic unit test tests/test_bronze_scheduler.py (pytestmark = pytest.mark.unit; tmp_path; monkeypatch; no Docker/network), covering: (a) MinIO unreachable -> _run_batch returns 'degraded', does NOT raise, does NOT construct RawLander, and writes a manifest with status='degraded' and storage_reachable=False under tmp_path; (b) the schedule loop body swallows a batch exception and keeps looping (patch schedule.run_pending to raise once then assert the loop continues / does not propagate). Follow the monkeypatch+fixed-clock style of tests/test_bronze_live_check.py and tests/test_infra_minio.py.
10. Update docs/GAP_REGISTER.md GAP-019 row status to in_progress with the changed files, then to closed only after the verification command passes; add a row to the Test Failure Mapping table. Update docs/CODEMAP.md run.py line (currently line 40) to mention the degrade-on-unreachable-storage + evidence-manifest behavior and the new deploy/ + docs/OPERATIONS.md artifacts.
11. Run the full verification command set (see verification field), confirm green, and record the result line in docs/VERIFICATION.md and the GAP_REGISTER Test Failure Mapping table.

**Files to touch:** `src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/run.py`  `docker-compose.yml`  `deploy/railway-bronze-stats.service`  `deploy/railway-bronze-stats.timer`  `deploy/railway-bronze-news.service`  `deploy/railway-bronze-news.timer`  `tests/test_bronze_scheduler.py`  `docs/OPERATIONS.md`  `docs/INDEX.md`  `README.md`  `docs/VERIFICATION.md`  `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md`  `docs/CODEMAP.md`

**Definition of Done (contract).**
- [ ] A MinIO-unreachable boot of `python -m railway_lakehouse.bronze.run schedule` does NOT raise/crash: it logs a clear warning, writes a status='degraded' manifest under output/evidence/scheduler/, and the schedule loop still starts.
- [ ] run_stats()/run_news() (and the shared _run_batch) never raise on an unreachable MinIO and never construct RawLander in that case; per-source ingest failures are caught and recorded, not propagated.
- [ ] The schedule loop body is wrapped so a single batch exception is logged and the loop continues (cadence survives one bad run).
- [ ] A deployable host exists and is committed: a `scheduler` service in docker-compose.yml (depends_on minio, restart: unless-stopped, runs `... bronze.run schedule`) AND systemd .service/.timer units under deploy/ (Persistent=true) with a documented cron alternative — restart-safe cadence no longer lives only in memory.
- [ ] A runbook line exists: docs/OPERATIONS.md documents the deploy command(s) and the degradation contract, is linked from docs/INDEX.md, and README.md carries a one-line pointer.
- [ ] tests/test_bronze_scheduler.py is a deterministic unit test (no Docker/network, tmp_path + monkeypatch) that asserts (a) unreachable-MinIO -> degraded, no raise, manifest written, no RawLander constructed, and (b) the loop swallows a batch exception and keeps looping.
- [ ] Raw Bronze write semantics are unchanged: RawLander.__init__ and RawLander.land are not modified; no Silver/Gold/LLM/numeric code touched.
- [ ] `python -m pytest -q` is green (prior count was 87 passed; expect 87 + the new scheduler tests) and `python -m compileall -q src tests` passes.
- [ ] docs/GAP_REGISTER.md GAP-019 is moved to closed with evidence, and a Test Failure Mapping row + a docs/VERIFICATION.md result block record the passing command output.

**Verify:** `python -m pytest -q tests/test_bronze_scheduler.py  &&  python -m pytest -q -m unit  &&  python -m pytest -q  &&  python -m compileall -q src tests  &&  git diff --check`

**Pitfalls.** "Hard rules: raw Bronze stays immutable — do not change RawLander.land or its bytes-then-meta write order (lander.py:86-89); the fix is a reachability preflight + batch wrapper, NOT a change to landing semantics. All evidence/manifests go under output/ (use output/evidence/scheduler/), never the repo root or eduagent/. No LLM, no numeric rewriting, no fabricated data — manifests record only what actually happened (real status/error strings, real landed counts). Tests must not depend on coursework/ data: use tmp_path + monkeypatch a fake RawLander/ s3fs that raises a connection error; do NOT hit a real MinIO or the network, and do NOT call the real ingest functions (they make HTTP calls). Make _storage_reachable's probe cheap and fully wrapped in try/except — a bare s3fs.exists can raise several botocore exception types; catch broadly (Exception) and stringify, mirroring scripts/minio_smoke.py:121-136. Beware the boot double-run: today schedule mode runs both batches at boot AND on cadence; keep that behavior but ensure the boot run uses the degrade path. Do not let the new compose `scheduler` service crash-loop: depends_on createbuckets and the degraded-boot path together prevent the historical crash. Keep run_stats()/run_news() as named wrappers so docs/CODEMAP.md, WIRING.md, and any future GAP-005 PR that calls them still work. Persistent=true on systemd timers is what actually makes missed runs fire after downtime — without it a reboot still skips the window."


## MID

### GAP-005 — Wire KSH, Statistik Austria, and UIC into the Bronze scheduler through the RawLander contract (keep historical GDELT one-off)

`MID` · level **bronze** · effort **S** · depends on: none — adapters ksh.py/statistik_austria.py/uic.py and RawLander already exist and are live-proven (GAP-010 evidence); GAP-001/002/003 (package/import root) are closed. This is independent of GAP-006 (Silver parsers) and GAP-007 (Gold).

**Build:** Add the three live-proven national/UIC stats adapters to bronze/run.py's run_stats() so every configured stats source lands through the same RawLander contract, with a deterministic mocked-lander test proving each adapter is invoked exactly once.

**Context.** Bronze is the ingestion layer of the railway lakehouse (web sources -> Bronze -> Silver -> Gold -> Spark -> report). The scheduler at src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/run.py is the orchestration entrypoint that drives source adapters via the RawLander (the only component allowed to write the Bronze bucket). Eight Bronze adapters exist and KSH/Statistik Austria/UIC are live-proven (raw bytes landed, manifests committed under output/evidence/), but run_stats() still only schedules Eurostat + World Bank, so the "automatic updates" requirement is unmet for the national agencies. This is the GAP-005 row (open, Workstream C - Bronze Owner, sync point S2 data contracts) and TASKS.md slug bronze/scheduler-wiring (Wave 5). It is pure orchestration: it must NOT touch raw landing semantics or parse anything (parsing is GAP-006/Silver).

**Problem.** src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/run.py:21 imports only `eurostat, worldbank, gdelt, rss_media`. run_stats() (run.py:28-34) calls `eurostat.ingest(lander)` and `worldbank.ingest(lander)` then logs the placeholder comment `# GAP-005: national agencies are present but not scheduled yet.` (run.py:33). The three adapters ksh.py, statistik_austria.py, uic.py all exist with the matching contract `ingest(lander, session=None) -> int` (ksh.py:139, statistik_austria.py:163, uic.py:112), identical in shape to the scheduled eurostat.ingest (eurostat.py:71) and worldbank.ingest (worldbank.py:112). They are simply never imported or called. Historical GDELT lives in past_recordings.py (ingest at past_recordings.py:220) but its docstring (past_recordings.py:1-30) and the prior decision record both state it is a one-off deep-history seed (default target 50,000 articles) that must stay opt-in, not run on the weekly cadence. There is currently ZERO test coverage of run.py (no test file imports bronze.run, run_stats, or run_news), so the scheduler's source set is entirely unverified. The GAP-005 closure criterion is: "Scheduler imports and runs every configured source through the same RawLander contract." Verification command: `python -m pytest -q -m unit`.

**Steps.**
1. Re-read the contract surface before editing: run.py:28-42 (run_stats/run_news), and confirm the ingest signatures with `grep -rn "def ingest" src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/sources/*.py` — eurostat/worldbank/ksh/statistik_austria/uic all share `ingest(lander, session=None)`; gdelt and past_recordings differ (extra kwargs). This is why only the five stats adapters are safely uniform to chain in run_stats().

3. Edit run_stats() (run.py:28-34): after `worldbank.ingest(lander)` add `ksh.ingest(lander)`, `statistik_austria.ingest(lander)`, `uic.ingest(lander)`. Replace the stale placeholder comment at run.py:33 with a brief note explaining that historical GDELT is a deliberate one-off seed run via `python -m railway_lakehouse.bronze.sources.past_recordings`, not part of the yearly stats cadence. Keep the existing `=== Bronze STATS batch ===` log lines.

Define a FakeLander recording (source, dataset_id) tuples or just call counts — DO NOT construct a real RawLander (its __init__ at lander.py:44-54 opens an s3fs.S3FileSystem and would hit network/MinIO). Use monkeypatch to replace `RawLander` in the run module namespace with a no-arg fake, OR pass nothing and instead monkeypatch each `<module>.ingest` to a recording stub.

**Verify:** `python -m pytest -q tests/test_bronze_run.py && python -m pytest -q -m unit && python -m pytest -q && python -m compileall -q src tests`

**Pitfalls.** "DO NOT instantiate a real RawLander in tests: RawLander.__init__ (lander.py:44-54) builds an s3fs.S3FileSystem and calls self.s3.exists/mkdir, which requires MinIO/network — monkeypatch run.RawLander to a no-arg fake. No parsing, decoding, or casting of source bytes (that is Silver/GAP-006). Keep ingest call order deterministic in run_stats so the order-explicit assertion is stable. ### GAP-014 — Force UTF-8 on the live (s3/MinIO) text read in pipeline._read_text

`MID` · level **pipeline** · effort **S** · depends on: none (self-contained; fsspec==2024.6.1 is already a direct dependency in pyproject.toml so memory:// is available without new packages)

**Build:** Make the s3/non-Path branch of `_read_text` decode bytes as UTF-8 explicitly so live MinIO news reads match the UTF-8-forced local branch, and add a deterministic fsspec `memory://` unit test proving an exact round-trip regardless of OS locale.

**Context.** `_read_text` is the text reader for Bronze news artifacts (RSS XML and GDELT/RSS JSON) consumed by `_read_bronze_news` in the Silver-news stage of the Bronze→Silver→Gold pipeline (`src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py`). News content is overwhelmingly non-ASCII (Hungarian/German rail terms like "MÁV", "vasút", "ÖBB", typographic quotes, the euro sign). The local-fixture branch already forces `encoding="utf-8"`, but the live MinIO/s3 branch does not — so the two read paths diverge and the live path corrupts data on any machine whose locale is not UTF-8. This is a Wave-5 robustness gap (GAP-014, medium) sitting next to GAP-020 (the s3 read branches have no deterministic coverage at all); fixing it also lays the first fsspec-memory test pattern for that branch.

**Problem.** `src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py:277-281`, function `_read_text(lander, path)`:

```python
def _read_text(lander, path) -> str:
    if isinstance(path, Path):
        return path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")        # line 279: local branch, UTF-8 forced
    with lander.s3.open(path, "r") as f:               # line 280: s3 branch, text mode, NO encoding
        return f.read()                                # line 281
```

Line 280 opens the object in text mode (`"r"`) with no `encoding=` argument. fsspec/s3fs wrap the binary stream in `io.TextIOWrapper(encoding=None)`, which falls back to `locale.getpreferredencoding(False)`. On the current machine that is **cp1251**, so UTF-8 news bytes are silently mis-decoded (mojibake) or, for byte sequences invalid under the locale codec, raise `UnicodeDecodeError` and abort the Silver-news batch. Verified two ways on this machine (cp1251):
- Raw fsspec: writing `'Accént — "quotes" €'` as UTF-8 then reading back via `fs.open(path, 'r')` returns a corrupted string (roundtrip == False); reading with `encoding='utf-8'` returns roundtrip == True.
- Through the real function: `pipeline._read_text(SimpleNamespace(s3=fsspec.filesystem("memory")), "/bronze/news/rss/a.xml")` on UTF-8 bytes `'MÁV vasút — ÖBB "investment" €5'` returns roundtrip == False, repr starts `'MÁV vasút — Ö'`.

This is the **only** text-mode (`"r"`) s3 read in the file. The sibling `_read_tsv` s3 branch at `pipeline.py:273` opens `"rb"` (binary) and is unaffected. The defect is purely live-path: deterministic fixture/integration tests use the `Path` branch (line 279), so the full suite is green and the bug is invisible — exactly why a test on the s3 branch is required.

**Steps.**
1. Read `src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py:277-281` to confirm `_read_text` is unchanged from this spec (the s3 branch still uses `lander.s3.open(path, "r")` with no encoding).
2. Fix the s3 branch to force UTF-8. Preferred (matches the binary pattern already used by `_read_tsv` and avoids any TextIOWrapper-locale surprise): open in binary and decode explicitly — change line 280-281 to `with lander.s3.open(path, "rb") as f:` / `return f.read().decode("utf-8")`. Acceptable alternative: keep text mode but pass the encoding, `lander.s3.open(path, "r", encoding="utf-8")`. Both round-trip correctly under fsspec memory:// and s3fs; use the binary+decode form for symmetry with `_read_tsv`. Do not touch the `Path` branch (line 279) — it is already correct.
3. Add a deterministic unit test to `tests/test_pipeline_gaps.py` (it already imports `SimpleNamespace`, `pytest`, and `railway_lakehouse.pipeline`). NOTE: that module sets `pytestmark = pytest.mark.integration` at file scope, but GAP-014's closure command is `-m unit`. To get a unit-marked test, add it with an explicit `@pytest.mark.unit` decorator AND counteract the module-level integration mark — simplest is to put the new test in a NEW file `tests/test_pipeline_read_text.py` with `pytestmark = pytest.mark.unit` (cleaner, no marker conflict). Prefer the new file.
4. In `tests/test_pipeline_read_text.py`: build a lander with no `bronze_root` and an injected fsspec memory filesystem so the call takes the s3/non-Path branch: `import fsspec`; `fs = fsspec.filesystem("memory")`; `lander = SimpleNamespace(s3=fs)`. Use a unique in-memory path per test (memory:// is process-global) e.g. `path = "/gap014/news/rss/a.xml"`.
5. Seed UTF-8 bytes that exercise accents AND typographic characters (the GAP closure criterion): `text = 'MÁV vasút — ÖBB “investment” €5 – café'` (em dash, smart quotes, euro sign, en dash, accented e). Write them as raw bytes: `with fs.open(path, "wb") as f: f.write(text.encode("utf-8"))`.
6. Assert an EXACT round-trip independent of locale: `assert railway_lakehouse.pipeline._read_text(lander, path) == text`. To make the locale-independence explicit and guard against regressions on any CI runner, also force a non-UTF-8 preferred encoding for the duration of the test via monkeypatch: `monkeypatch.setattr(locale, "getpreferredencoding", lambda do_setlocale=True: "cp1251")` (import `locale`). The binary+decode fix passes regardless; the monkeypatch documents intent and makes the test fail loudly if someone reverts to locale-dependent text mode. Keep the assertion the load-bearing check.
7. (Optional, strengthens against GAP-020 overlap) add a second assertion in the same test that a Path-based read of an equivalent UTF-8 file in `tmp_path` returns the same string, proving local/live parity. Keep it lightweight; the s3-branch round-trip is the required check.
8. Run the verification command (below) and confirm the new test passes and the full suite stays green (87 passed baseline + new test).
9. Update docs: add a one-line entry to the `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md` Test Failure Mapping table referencing GAP-014 with the passing `-m unit` result, and flip GAP-014's `Status` to `closed` with a dated evidence note in its row (the register convention: closed = verification command passed and evidence recorded). Do NOT mark closed until the command actually passes.
10. Run `python -m compileall -q src tests` and `git diff --check` (repo hygiene gates used throughout this project's evidence log).

**Files to touch:** `src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py (fix `_read_text` s3 branch, lines 280-281)`  `tests/test_pipeline_read_text.py (new file; deterministic fsspec memory:// unit test, `pytestmark = pytest.mark.unit`)`  `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md (flip GAP-014 row to closed; add a Test Failure Mapping entry)`

**Definition of Done (contract).**
- [ ] `pipeline._read_text` decodes the s3/non-Path branch as UTF-8 explicitly (binary `open(path, "rb")` + `.decode("utf-8")`, or `open(path, "r", encoding="utf-8")`); the `Path` branch is unchanged.
- [ ] A new deterministic unit test drives `_read_text` through the s3/non-Path branch using an injected fsspec `memory://` filesystem (lander = `SimpleNamespace(s3=fs)`, no `bronze_root`) seeded with UTF-8 bytes containing accents AND typographic characters (em dash, smart quotes, euro sign), and asserts an exact string round-trip.
- [ ] The test proves locale-independence: it passes even when `locale.getpreferredencoding` is monkeypatched to a non-UTF-8 codec (e.g. cp1251).
- [ ] The new test is collected by `python -m pytest -q -m unit` (carries the `unit` marker, not `integration`).
- [ ] `python -m pytest -q -m unit` passes including the new test; `python -m pytest -q` stays green (no regressions; prior baseline 87 passed).
- [ ] No Docker, MinIO, or network is required to run the test.
- [ ] GAP-014's row in `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md` is set to `closed` with a dated evidence line, and a Test Failure Mapping row records the passing `-m unit` command — only after the command actually passed.
- [ ] `python -m compileall -q src tests` passes and `git diff --check` is clean.
- [ ] Raw Bronze immutability respected: this changes only how bytes are decoded on read; no Bronze write path, no re-encoding, no numeric/stat rewriting touched.

**Verify:** `python -m pytest -q -m unit (must include and pass the new tests/test_pipeline_read_text.py; then confirm no regressions with `python -m pytest -q`, `python -m compileall -q src tests`, and `git diff --check`)`

**Pitfalls.** ["`tests/test_pipeline_gaps.py` sets `pytestmark = pytest.mark.integration` at module scope — adding the test there would mark it `integration`, but GAP-014's closure command is `-m unit`. Use a NEW file `tests/test_pipeline_read_text.py` with `pytestmark = pytest.mark.unit` to avoid the marker mismatch.", "fsspec `memory://` is process-global and persists across tests within a run; use a unique path per test (e.g. `/gap014/...`) or clean up, or a later test could see stale bytes.", "Do NOT change the `Path` branch (line 279) — it already forces UTF-8 and the green fixture/integration tests depend on it; the bug is exclusively the s3 branch (line 280).", "Prefer binary `open(path, \"rb\")` + `.decode(\"utf-8\")` over text-mode `open(..., \"r\", encoding=\"utf-8\")`: it mirrors `_read_tsv` (line 273), and some fsspec versions/backends route the `encoding=` kwarg inconsistently through `open`/`_open` — decoding the bytes yourself is unambiguous.", "This is a read-side decode fix only. Do NOT alter how Bronze bytes are written/landed (raw Bronze stays immutable), and do NOT introduce any LLM or value rewriting — strings are returned verbatim, just correctly decoded.", "Don't fabricate or hardcode coursework data in the test — synthesize the UTF-8 string inline and write it to memory:// (no `coursework/` or `output/` inputs).", "GAP-020 is a broader sibling (full s3-branch parity incl. gzip-over-s3 and the no-backend ValueError). Keep this PR scoped to `_read_text`/encoding; don't expand into GAP-020's surface, but the fsspec-memory lander pattern you add here is the reusable harness for it.", "The GAP register cites the function span `pipeline.py:277-281`; the actual buggy call is line 280 — cite line 280 in the closure note to be precise."]

### GAP-015 — Gold: normalize stats to canonical units before conflict-resolution and pivot

`MID` · level **gold** · effort **M** · depends on: none (GAP-015 is self-contained). Related but not blocking: GAP-013 (live path will start feeding both World Bank and Eurostat to Gold, the exact collision this guard protects) and GAP-016 (deterministic news schema) both touch gold/build.py — coordinate to avoid merge conflicts in that file, but neither must land first.

**Build:** Add a deterministic unit-normalization step in the Gold stats path so the unit column is honored (differently-scaled sources are converted to one canonical unit per feature, or the row is quarantined) instead of being silently dropped at pivot.

**Context.** Gold is the ML-ready (geo, year) feature matrix that Spark and the report consume, so a unit defect here silently corrupts every downstream deliverable. The Silver layer deliberately keeps each value in its source/native unit and tags a `unit` column (StatFact), explicitly deferring normalization to Gold: silver/config.py:25-26 ("Units are the canonical unit each feature is normalized to in Gold") and silver/schema.py:14 ("unit: source unit string (normalized later in Gold)"). That promised Gold step does not exist. GAP-013 is making the live path read both World Bank and Eurostat, so the day two differently-scaled sources both reach Gold for one feature, conflict resolution will silently mix scales — this gap is the guardrail for that.

**Problem.** The `unit` column is carried all the way into Gold (it survives merge_sources at silver/stats/merge.py:222-227 as one of the 8 StatFact columns) but Gold never reads it. Concretely: (1) resolve_stat_conflicts (gold/build.py:37-50) breaks a same-(geo,year,feature) collision purely by source_system priority (SOURCE_PRIORITY at gold/build.py:30) and keeps one row's value with no regard for its unit — so for one feature, HU-2020 might resolve to eurostat and AT-2020 to worldbank, producing a column whose rows are in different scales. (2) pivot_stats (gold/build.py:53-62) pivots values="value" only and drops unit entirely, so the magnitude ambiguity is baked into the matrix with no record of which unit each cell is in. The two stats readers actively produce divergent native units for the same canonical feature: read_eurostat_tsv sets unit="eurostat_native" (silver/stats/merge.py:71) and read_worldbank_json sets unit="worldbank_native" (silver/stats/merge.py:83); e.g. World Bank rail_freight_tonne_km (IS.RRS.GOOD.MT.K6) is reported in millions of tonne-km while Eurostat freight series are in thousands of tonnes — a ~1e3-1e6 scale gap that is currently merged as if identical. Docs compound the confusion: docs/DATA_CONTRACTS.md:100-116 Gold contract does not mention units at all, contradicting the Silver config/schema "normalized later in Gold" claim.

**Steps.**
1. Reproduce the defect first (TDD red): add a unit test in tests/test_gold_unit_normalization.py that builds a stats_long frame with ONE feature (rail_freight_tonne_km) from two sources for the SAME (geo, year) where the native values differ only by a known scale factor (e.g. worldbank value=5.0 unit='worldbank_native', eurostat value=5000.0 unit='eurostat_native'), runs the current pivot_stats, and asserts the resolved magnitude is canonical. Confirm it FAILS today (pivot keeps whichever source ranks higher, unconverted).
2. Decide the canonical-unit policy explicitly and deterministically (no LLM, per Hard Rules). In silver/config.py add a CANONICAL_UNITS mapping feature_key -> canonical unit label (e.g. 'rail_freight_tonne_km' -> 'tonne_km', 'rail_network_length_km' -> 'km', 'rail_passenger_km' -> 'passenger_km'), small and bounded, mirroring CANONICAL_FEATURES.
3. Define a deterministic conversion table keyed by (native_unit, feature) -> multiplicative factor to the canonical unit, as a literal dict in gold/build.py (e.g. _UNIT_FACTORS = {('worldbank_native','rail_freight_tonne_km'): 1.0, ('eurostat_native','rail_freight_tonne_km'): <factor>, ('native','rail_passengers'): 1.0, ...}). Where a (source,feature) native unit is genuinely unknown, do NOT guess: quarantine it (step 5). This table is the single reviewable source of truth.
4. Add normalize_units(stats_long) in gold/build.py that runs BEFORE resolve_stat_conflicts: for each row look up the factor by (unit, feature), multiply value deterministically (pure vectorized pandas), set unit to the canonical unit. Wire it into pivot_stats so the order is normalize -> resolve_conflicts -> pivot. Log a per-(source,feature,factor) normalized row count.
5. Handle the conflict/quarantine case: when a (source,feature) pair has no entry in the conversion table, drop those rows from the pivot and log a WARNING with the count and offending (source,feature,unit) tuples (mirror the 'merge: kept N/M rows' logging at silver/stats/merge.py:221). The step-1 test should accept EITHER a single canonical magnitude OR a quarantined conflict per the GAP-015 closure wording.
6. Keep call paths intact: build_gold (gold/build.py:127) calls pivot_stats (line 131) which now normalizes internally; do not change build_from_silver's signature in gold/run.py:23. Add identity factor 1.0 for unit='native' on the features the legacy fixtures touch so test_gold_characterization.py (test_resolve_stat_conflicts_honors_source_priority, test_pivot_stats_produces_geo_year_rows) stays green.
7. Reconcile docs with code: update docs/DATA_CONTRACTS.md Gold section (lines 100-116) to state Gold normalizes each feature to its canonical unit before pivot and quarantines un-reconcilable units (canonical unit per feature defined in silver/config.py); ensure the silver/config.py:25-26 and silver/schema.py:14 'normalized in Gold' claims now match real code.
8. Run the verification command and the full suite; record a new row in docs/GAP_REGISTER.md Test Failure Mapping and update GAP-015 status with evidence.

**Files to touch:** `C:\Users\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\Documents\tmp\ai-masters\coursework\bigdata\course_proj\src\railway_lakehouse\gold\build.py`  `C:\Users\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\Documents\tmp\ai-masters\coursework\bigdata\course_proj\src\railway_lakehouse\silver\config.py`  `C:\Users\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\Documents\tmp\ai-masters\coursework\bigdata\course_proj\tests\test_gold_unit_normalization.py`  `C:\Users\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\Documents\tmp\ai-masters\coursework\bigdata\course_proj\docs\DATA_CONTRACTS.md`  `C:\Users\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\Documents\tmp\ai-masters\coursework\bigdata\course_proj\docs\GAP_REGISTER.md`

**Definition of Done (contract).**
- [ ] A new deterministic unit test at tests/test_gold_unit_normalization.py is marked pytest.mark.unit, uses only in-test fixtures (no coursework/ or output/ data, no network), and passes.
- [ ] The test feeds a worldbank-vs-eurostat collision on ONE feature (differently-scaled native values for the same geo+year) and asserts EITHER (a) a single canonical-unit magnitude in the resulting matrix, OR (b) the conflicting rows are quarantined (dropped with a logged warning) — matching the GAP-015 closure wording.
- [ ] gold/build.py contains a deterministic normalize_units step that runs before resolve_stat_conflicts and pivot; it reads the unit column, applies a literal (unit,feature)->factor table, and never invokes an LLM or rewrites numbers non-deterministically.
- [ ] silver/config.py exposes an explicit CANONICAL_UNITS mapping (feature -> canonical unit) consistent with CANONICAL_FEATURES.
- [ ] Un-reconcilable (source,feature,unit) rows are quarantined with a logged count, not silently mixed into the matrix.
- [ ] All pre-existing tests pass unchanged: tests/test_gold_characterization.py (incl. test_resolve_stat_conflicts_honors_source_priority, test_pivot_stats_produces_geo_year_rows) and tests/test_silver_stats_integration.py remain green.
- [ ] docs/DATA_CONTRACTS.md Gold section documents the unit-normalization+quarantine behavior; the silver/config.py:25-26 and silver/schema.py:14 'normalized in Gold' claims now agree with code (docs and code unit claims agree).

- [ ] docs/GAP_REGISTER.md Test Failure Mapping has a new row recording the passing verification command and GAP-015 status is updated.

**Pitfalls.** HARD RULE: numeric stat merges stay deterministic — conversion factors MUST be a literal reviewable table; do NOT call Ollama/generate_json or any LLM to infer scales or rewrite numbers. Do not touch or regenerate raw Bronze. The existing test_gold_characterization fixtures use unit='native' (not eurostat_native/worldbank_native) — if you only add *_native entries you will break those tests with NaN/dropped rows, so add an identity factor (1.0) for 'native' on the features they exercise (rail_passengers). resolve_stat_conflicts and pivot_stats are imported and called directly by tests, so preserve their signatures and the (geo,year,feature)->one-value semantics; insert normalization upstream rather than rewriting the conflict policy. The pivot at gold/build.py:58-60 uses aggfunc='first' on values='value' only — if two same-(geo,year,feature) rows survive with the same canonical unit, conflict-resolution must still pick exactly one (keep the source-priority tiebreak). Beware real scale gaps: World Bank tonne-km (IS.RRS.GOOD.MT.K6) is in millions while Eurostat freight is in thousands — a wrong factor silently corrupts the headline real Gold (2,968x4). Eurostat currently does not reach Gold (SDMX header issue, GAP-013), so a true two-source real-feature collision is not yet observable in the live pipeline; the deterministic test is the only reliable guard, which is why it is mandatory in the DoD.

### GAP-016 — Make the Gold news feature schema deterministic by reindexing event-type and operator pivots to the canonical vocabularies

`MID` · level **gold** · effort **S** · depends on: none (independent of GAP-012/013/014). GAP-015 (Gold unit normalization) also touches gold/build.py but a different code path (stats pivot, not aggregate_news), so do GAP-016 first or coordinate to avoid a merge conflict in the same file.

**Build:** In aggregate_news (gold/build.py), reindex the event-type and operator pivots to the full NEWS_EVENT_TYPES and KNOWN_OPERATORS vocabularies (filling absent categories with 0) so the emitted column set is identical across any two batches.

**Context.** Gold (src/railway_lakehouse/gold/build.py) builds the final ML-ready (geo, year) feature matrix consumed by the report, the Spark coverage job, and any downstream model. Its news block derives per-(country, year) features (event counts, operator mentions, sentiment, money) from validated Silver NewsFeature rows. This is the deterministic, no-LLM Gold stage, so under the repo Hard Rules numeric merges stay deterministic and no LLM may rewrite numbers; the fix is pure pandas reshaping with zero change to the actual counts. The bug matters because a non-deterministic schema breaks schema-stable Parquet writes, column-aligned concat/join of Gold across runs, and any model expecting a fixed feature vector.

**Problem.** In src/railway_lakehouse/gold/build.py the news aggregation has two structural non-determinism defects, both confirmed by reproduction (disjoint batches A={event=investment, op=RailCargo} and B={event=accident, op=GYSEV} produce disjoint column sets; set(columns) are not equal).

1. Event-type pivot (build.py:99-105): pivot_table(..., columns="event_type", ...) only emits a column for each event type PRESENT in the batch. The follow-up rename at build.py:105 ( ev = ev.rename(columns={e: f"news_n_{e}" for e in NEWS_EVENT_TYPES}) ) only renames event types that already exist as columns; it never creates the missing ones. A batch with only investment yields just news_n_investment; a batch with only accident yields just news_n_accident.

2. Operator pivot (build.py:107-117): the entire block is guarded by `if not ops.empty:` (build.py:110). When no KNOWN_OPERATORS appear in the batch, zero news_op_* columns are emitted. When only some appear, only those operators get columns, because the rename at build.py:116 ( opc.rename(columns={o: f"news_op_{o}" for o in KNOWN_OPERATORS}) ) has the same rename-only-present-columns flaw.

3. build_gold (build.py:144-148) only fills NaN with 0 for news_ columns that already exist in gold.columns, so it cannot recover the missing canonical columns; it just zero-fills whatever survived. NEWS_EVENT_TYPES (config.py:42-45) has 10 entries and KNOWN_OPERATORS (config.py:46) has 6 entries (MAV, GYSEV, OBB, Westbahn, RailCargo, other) including a shared name "other" that is safe because the prefixes differ (news_n_other vs news_op_other).

**Steps.**
1. Reproduce the bug first (red baseline): run the snippet in `verification` and confirm set(aggregate_news(A).columns) != set(aggregate_news(B).columns) on disjoint event/operator batches.
2. Open src/railway_lakehouse/gold/build.py and locate the event-type pivot at lines 99-105 inside aggregate_news.
3. After building the event pivot `ev` (and resetting its index), force the full canonical event vocabulary BEFORE renaming. The clean approach: keep the pivot, then reindex the pivoted category columns to NEWS_EVENT_TYPES with fill_value=0. Concretely, after build.py:103 (the .reset_index()) set the index back to [country, year], reindex columns to NEWS_EVENT_TYPES (columns=NEWS_EVENT_TYPES, fill_value=0) so every canonical event type is a column even when absent, then reset_index and rename to news_n_<event>. Equivalent and simpler: make event_type a Categorical with categories=NEWS_EVENT_TYPES before the pivot and pass observed=False so pivot_table emits all categories. Pick one and keep it deterministic.
4. Fix the operator block at lines 107-117 the same way. Remove the `if not ops.empty:` early-out so operator columns are ALWAYS produced. Build the per-(country, year) operator counts and reindex/ensure all KNOWN_OPERATORS are present as columns with 0 for absent ones, then rename to news_op_<op> and merge onto agg. When the exploded ops frame is empty, construct a zero-filled operator block aligned to the agg (country, year) keys so the news_op_* columns still appear with all-zero counts.
5. Ensure the operator and event columns are integer-typed and zero-filled (not NaN) on the merge so the deterministic-schema columns are also deterministically dtyped; this matches the existing build_gold zero-fill intent (build.py:144-148).
6. Keep column ORDER deterministic too: emit news_n_<event> in NEWS_EVENT_TYPES order and news_op_<op> in KNOWN_OPERATORS order so set-equality AND a stable left-to-right order both hold. The DoD only requires set-equality, but stable order is free and prevents Parquet schema churn.
7. Do NOT change the sentiment/count/money aggregations (build.py:91-97) or the geo rename (build.py:120). Do not touch the empty-input early returns (build.py:82-88) which legitimately return only [geo, year] when there is no qualifying news row.
8. Add a deterministic unit test test_aggregate_news_schema_is_deterministic in tests/test_gold_characterization.py (pytestmark already = pytest.mark.unit at line 7). Assert set(aggregate_news(A).columns) == set(aggregate_news(B).columns) for disjoint event/operator batches, and assert every news_n_<event> for e in NEWS_EVENT_TYPES and every news_op_<op> for o in KNOWN_OPERATORS is present. Also assert the counts are unchanged (e.g. A still has news_n_investment == 1 and news_op_RailCargo == 1, and a canonical-but-absent column like news_n_strike == 0).
9. Run the unit suite and confirm green; spot-check the existing test_aggregate_news_counts_events_sentiment_money_and_operators (build/test lines 63-109) still passes unchanged.

Update docs/DATA_CONTRACTS.md Gold Contract (lines 100-116): state that the Gold news block always emits one news_n_<event> column per NEWS_EVENT_TYPES and one news_op_<op> column per KNOWN_OPERATORS, zero-filled when absent, so the news schema is run-independent. Update docs/GAP_REGISTER.md GAP-016 row to closed with the verification command + result, and add a row to the Test Failure Mapping table.

### GAP-018 — Bound pandas/pyarrow majors, commit a constraints lockfile, and add a version-guard test

`MID` · level **ops** · effort **S** · depends on: none (Wave-1, self-contained), Coordinate-only with GAP-017: both edit pyproject.toml but in disjoint regions (GAP-018 = [project].dependencies lines 10-19; GAP-017 = [project.optional-dependencies].spark lines 26-28). Merge order does not matter; avoid a textual conflict by not reformatting unrelated lines.

**Build:** Pin pandas/pyarrow to the validated major window in pyproject.toml, commit a constraints.txt that locks the full runtime stack, and add tests/test_env_versions.py that fails when the installed pandas/pyarrow major drifts outside the graded window.

**Context.** This is an ops/reproducibility guard, not a data-path change. It protects the environment the whole Bronze/Silver/Gold pipeline and its 87-test suite run against. STATE_AND_ROADMAP.md:288 records the validated/graded environment as Python 3.14.0 / pandas 3.0.3 / pyarrow 24.0.0 with `python -m pytest -q` = 87 passed; pyproject.toml currently lets a fresh install resolve a different (e.g. future pandas 4.x / pyarrow 25+) stack silently. GAP-018 is Wave-1 work paired with GAP-017 (the Spark-extra pin) in docs/TASKS.md:121, and Contract A (TASKS.md:124-128) requires "a guard test fails on a wrong-major pandas/pyarrow" before Wave 2. Self-contained, one-session ops task with no dependency on the data layers.

**Problem.** Three concrete defects let a fresh checkout silently resolve a different stack than the graded one:

1. pyproject.toml:12-13 declares `pandas>=2.2` and `pyarrow>=15` with NO upper bound, so a clean `pip install -e ".[test]"` resolves whatever latest majors exist (future pandas 4.x, pyarrow 25+) that were never run against the suite. The validated window is pandas 2.2..3.x and pyarrow 15..24.x (installed today, confirmed via `pip freeze`: pandas 3.0.3, pyarrow 24.0.0; recorded at STATE_AND_ROADMAP.md:288).

2. No lockfile/constraints file exists anywhere in the repo. Verified: no poetry.lock, requirements*.txt, or constraints*.txt, and .gitignore (read in full) has no rule that would hide one. The S3 stack IS exact-pinned in pyproject (s3fs==2024.6.1, fsspec==2024.6.1, aiobotocore==2.13.1, botocore==1.34.131 at lines 15-18), but pandas, pyarrow, requests (>=2.31), schedule (>=1.2), and pytest (>=8.2) float, and transitive deps are entirely unpinned. So even the "pinned" subset can drift transitively.

3. No version-guard test exists. The closure command in GAP_REGISTER.md:46 is `pytest -q tests/test_env_versions.py`, but `tests/test_env_versions.py` does not exist (verified by directory listing). Nothing fails when a wrong-major pandas/pyarrow is installed.

Net effect: the "87 passed" evidence is only meaningful on one un-pinned, undocumented stack; a classmate or grader installing from a clean checkout has no guarantee of reproducing it, and no signal if they do not.

Out of scope for GAP-018 (do NOT touch): the `[spark]` extra `pyspark>=3.5` at pyproject.toml:26-28 is GAP-017's job; only coordinate so the two PRs do not collide on the same file region.

**Steps.**
1. 1. Capture the validated stack as ground truth. Run `python -m pip freeze` in the active env and record the exact versions of every pyproject runtime dependency plus their transitive deps. The validated core is already known: Python 3.14.0, pandas==3.0.3, pyarrow==24.0.0, requests==2.33.1, s3fs==2024.6.1, fsspec==2024.6.1, aiobotocore==2.13.1, botocore==1.34.131, schedule==1.2.2, pytest>=8.2. These are the numbers the constraints file and guard test must encode.
2. 2. Bound the floating majors in pyproject.toml:11-19. Change requires-python from `>=3.12` to a bounded range that includes the validated 3.14 (e.g. `>=3.12,<3.15`). Change line 12 `pandas>=2.2` -> `pandas>=2.2,<4` and line 13 `pyarrow>=15` -> `pyarrow>=15,<25`. Also bound `requests>=2.31` -> `requests>=2.31,<3` and `schedule>=1.2` -> `schedule>=1.2,<2` (optional but cheap consistency). Leave the four exact `==` S3 pins (lines 15-18) untouched. Do NOT modify the `[spark]` extra (lines 26-28) — that is GAP-017.
3. 3. Create a committed lock at repo root: `constraints.txt`. Populate it from the `pip freeze` of step 1, restricted to the runtime + test closure (exclude editable `-e` self-reference and obvious build-only/IDE noise). Pin each line with `==`. Add a header comment block stating: the date generated, the Python version it was frozen on (3.14.0), the exact regen command, and that it is the authoritative graded stack. Keep it deterministic and human-reviewable.
4. 4. Document the reproducible-install recipe. In README.md Quickstart (around lines 13-18) and docs/VERIFICATION.md 'Safe Checks Now' (around lines 127-137), add the constrained install form: `python -m pip install -e ".[test]" -c constraints.txt`. State plainly that `-c constraints.txt` reproduces the graded stack and that omitting it allows drift the guard test will catch.
5. 5. Add tests/test_env_versions.py. Mirror the conventions in tests/test_infra_minio.py: module-level `pytestmark = pytest.mark.unit`, `ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]`, no network, no Docker, no coursework/ data. The test must: (a) import pandas and pyarrow and read `pandas.__version__` / `pyarrow.__version__`; (b) parse the major (and for pandas the major.minor lower bound) and assert the installed major is inside the validated window (pandas >=2.2 and <4 major; pyarrow >=15 and <25), failing with a clear message naming the observed vs. allowed range on a wrong-major install; (c) assert the bounds it enforces are the SAME bounds declared in pyproject.toml — read pyproject.toml via `tomllib` (3.11+ stdlib, available on 3.14), extract the pandas/pyarrow specifiers from `[project].dependencies`, and assert they contain the upper bounds added in step 2, so the test and pyproject can never silently diverge; (d) assert a committed `constraints.txt` exists at ROOT and pins both `pandas==` and `pyarrow==` lines (so the lockfile cannot be deleted without a red test). Keep version parsing dependency-free (no `packaging` import unless already a transitive dep — prefer splitting on '.' and int()).
6. 6. Run the guard test and the full suite to confirm green on the validated stack: `python -m pytest -q tests/test_env_versions.py` then `python -m pytest -q`. Then prove it actually guards: temporarily monkeypatch or stub a wrong major in a scratch check (or reason via the assertion) to confirm a wrong-major pandas/pyarrow would fail — do this with a throwaway parametrized assertion in the test itself (e.g. a helper `_in_window(major, lo, hi)` unit-tested with an out-of-window value), so the negative case is permanently covered without needing a second environment.
7. 7. Verify resolution honors the bounds: `python -m pip install --dry-run -e ".[test]" -c constraints.txt` (pip 26.0.1 supports --dry-run) and confirm it would install pandas 3.x / pyarrow 24.x, not a future major. Record the dry-run line in docs/VERIFICATION.md.
8. 8. Update docs/GAP_REGISTER.md: move GAP-018 status from `open` toward `closed`/`in_progress` per repo convention, add a Test Failure Mapping row for `python -m pytest -q tests/test_env_versions.py` with the passed count, and note the constraints.txt path as evidence. Update docs/STATE_AND_ROADMAP.md and docs/TASKS.md Contract A checkbox only if the repo convention is to tick it on completion.

**Files to touch:** `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/pyproject.toml`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/constraints.txt`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/tests/test_env_versions.py`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/README.md`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/docs/VERIFICATION.md`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/docs/GAP_REGISTER.md`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/docs/STATE_AND_ROADMAP.md`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/docs/TASKS.md`

Run all three from C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj.`

**Pitfalls.** ["Do NOT widen or change the four exact S3 pins (s3fs/fsspec/aiobotocore/botocore at pyproject.toml:15-18) — they are deliberately coupled for the s3fs<->botocore<->aiobotocore compatibility matrix; loosening them reintroduces a resolution trap.", "Do NOT touch the [spark] extra — GAP-017 owns pyspark/delta-spark pinning; editing it causes a merge collision and scope creep.", "Set the pandas upper bound to `<4` (not `<3.1` or `==3.0.*`): the validated stack is 3.0.3 but the window legitimately spans 2.2..3.x, and over-tightening would break a classmate who validly has pandas 2.2. Likewise pyarrow `<25` keeps 15..24 valid.", "tomllib is stdlib only on Python 3.11+; this repo targets >=3.12 so it is safe — but read pyproject.toml as binary ('rb') for tomllib.load, not text.", "Parse versions without assuming `packaging` is installed (it may not be a direct dep); split on '.' and int() the major, and guard against non-numeric suffixes (e.g. release candidates).", "The guard test must derive its bounds from / cross-check against pyproject.toml so the two cannot silently diverge — a hardcoded duplicate window that drifts from pyproject is itself a future GAP.", "Keep the test deterministic and offline: read installed versions via the imported module `__version__`, not via subprocess pip calls (subprocess is slow, network-touching, and non-deterministic in CI).", "Hard Rules unaffected but respect them: no Bronze/data changes, no LLM, all artifacts already live in repo root/output/ — do not write evidence into output/runtime/ or any coursework/ path; the test uses only ROOT-relative repo files, no tmp_path fixture needed here since it reads committed config (mirror test_infra_minio.py which also reads ROOT files).", "Regenerate constraints.txt from the SAME interpreter the suite is validated on (3.14.0); freezing from a different Python could pin versions that do not match the graded run."]

### GAP-020 — Deterministic test coverage for the s3/MinIO Bronze read-back branch (fsspec memory://)

`MID` · level **tests** · effort **S** · depends on: none for the core s3-branch tests (fsspec==2024.6.1 already pinned in pyproject.toml; MemoryFileSystem confirmed importable), GAP-014 (UTF-8 `_read_text` fix at pipeline.py:280) is the only coupling: Test 6's UTF-8 read parity cannot pass until that one-line fix lands — bundle the fix here or xfail Test 6 with a GAP-014 reference

**Build:** Add a no-Docker unit test that drives the s3/non-Path branches of `_list_bronze_files`, `_read_tsv` (incl. gzip), and `_read_text` in pipeline.py through an injected fsspec `memory://` filesystem, asserting local/live read parity plus the no-backend `ValueError`.

**Context.** `src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py` is the Bronze->Silver->Gold driver. Its Bronze readers have two backends: a local `Path`/`bronze_root` branch (used by every committed fixture/integration test) and an s3/MinIO branch (`lander.s3`, an `s3fs.S3FileSystem`) used in live runs. Only the local branch is tested today; the s3 branch — `_list_bronze_files` glob+filter, `_read_tsv` (including gzip-over-s3), `_read_text`, and the no-backend `ValueError` — has zero deterministic coverage. This is the live read path that GAP-013 (live MinIO stats) and GAP-010 (live E2E) depend on, so it is currently the riskiest untested seam in the live lakehouse path, and it is fully testable offline via an injected fsspec `memory://` filesystem (no MinIO, no Docker).

**Problem.** The s3/non-Path branches in `src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py` are uncovered:
- `_list_bronze_files` s3 branch — pipeline.py:256-261: `if not hasattr(lander, "s3"): raise ValueError(...)` then `paths = sorted(lander.s3.glob(f"{BRONZE_BUCKET}/{domain}/{source or '*'}/*/ingest_date=*/*"))` filtered by `_is_data_file` (pipeline.py:264-266). Never exercised by a test; the no-backend `ValueError` (256-257) is also never asserted.
- `_read_tsv` s3 branch — pipeline.py:269-274: `if isinstance(path, Path): ... else: with lander.s3.open(path, "rb") as f: pd.read_csv(f, sep="\t", compression=compression)` where `compression = "gzip" if str(path).endswith(".gz") else None` (270). The gzip-over-s3 sub-branch is untested.
- `_read_text` s3 branch — pipeline.py:277-281: `else: with lander.s3.open(path, "r") as f: return f.read()`. Untested AND latently broken: opening in text mode (`"r"`) inherits the OS default encoding. Verified empirically on this machine (cp1251 locale): a UTF-8 payload through this branch raises `UnicodeDecodeError: 'charmap' codec can't decode byte 0x98` — this is the GAP-014 bug, and it makes UTF-8 read parity for `_read_text` impossible until that one-liner is fixed.
Empirically confirmed (offline) that `SimpleNamespace(s3=fsspec.filesystem("memory"))` reaches every one of these branches: `MemoryFileSystem.glob` returns leading-slash `str` paths (e.g. `/bronze/stats/eurostat/ds1/ingest_date=2026-06-22/passengers.tsv`), which are not `Path`, so `_read_tsv`/`_read_text` take the s3 branch; `_is_data_file`, `_dataset_id_from_path`, `_source_from_news_path` all parse those paths correctly; gzip-over-s3 reads back; and the bare-object `ValueError` fires.

**Steps.**
1. Read the target functions in `src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py`: `_list_bronze_files` (248-261), `_is_data_file` (264-266), `_read_tsv` (269-274), `_read_text` (277-281), and the callers `_read_bronze_eurostat` (178-189) and `_read_bronze_news` (213-237). Note the s3 glob pattern is rooted at `BRONZE_BUCKET` (pipeline.py:259) whereas the local branch is rooted at `bronze_root` (252) — the in-memory layout must be `bronze/<domain>/<source>/<dataset>/ingest_date=YYYY-MM-DD/<file>` so the `{BRONZE_BUCKET}/...` pattern matches.
2. Create `tests/test_pipeline_s3_readback.py` with `pytestmark = pytest.mark.unit`. Add a fixture/helper `_seed_memory_bronze()` that builds a fresh `fs = fsspec.filesystem('memory')` and, to avoid cross-test state leakage in the process-global MemoryFileSystem store, clears it first (`fs.store.clear(); fs.pseudo_dirs[:] = ['']` or delete the known keys). Write objects with `fs.pipe(path, bytes)` mirroring the committed fixture tree: a Eurostat `.tsv`, a gzip `.tsv.gz` (built with `gzip.GzipFile`), each with its `.meta.json` sidecar, plus a news `.xml` and a news `.json` with sidecars, all under `bronze/...` (no leading slash on write).
3. Inject the backend as `lander = SimpleNamespace(s3=fs)` (deliberately omitting `bronze_root` so the s3 branch is taken).
4. Test 1 — `_list_bronze_files` s3 branch + `_is_data_file` filtering: call `pipeline._list_bronze_files(lander, domain='stats', source='eurostat', include=lambda n: n.endswith(('.tsv', '.tsv.gz')))`; assert the `.tsv` and `.tsv.gz` paths are returned and the `.meta.json` sidecars are excluded.
5. Test 2 — no-backend `ValueError`: call `_list_bronze_files` with a backend object exposing neither `bronze_root` nor `s3` (a bare `object()` or empty class) and assert `pytest.raises(ValueError, match='bronze_root or s3')`.
6. Test 3 — gzip-over-s3 in `_read_tsv`: drive `_read_bronze_eurostat(lander)` (which routes through `_read_tsv` for both plain and gzip paths) OR call `_read_tsv` directly on the gzip s3 path; assert the returned DataFrame columns/rows match the decompressed TSV content.
7. Test 4 — local/live read parity for `_read_tsv`: read the SAME bytes via both backends — the committed local fixture (`SimpleNamespace(bronze_root=tests/fixtures/bronze)` -> Path branch) and an in-memory copy of those exact bytes (s3 branch) — and assert the two DataFrames are equal with `pandas.testing.assert_frame_equal`. This proves the two branches agree, which is the GAP-020 closure criterion.
8. Test 5 — `_read_text` s3 branch parity on ASCII: drive `_read_bronze_news(lander, limit=...)` or `_read_text` directly against the in-memory `.xml`/`.json` and assert the text round-trips and the resulting article dicts match the local-branch result for the same bytes.
9. Test 6 — `_read_text` UTF-8 parity (the GAP-014 reconciliation): seed an `.xml`/`.json` containing UTF-8-only characters (accents + typographic quotes), drive the s3 branch, and assert an exact UTF-8 round-trip independent of locale. This test will FAIL against current `pipeline.py:280` (`open(path, 'r')`), so apply the minimal GAP-014 fix in the same PR: change `_read_text` s3 branch to read bytes and decode UTF-8 explicitly — `with lander.s3.open(path, 'rb') as f: return f.read().decode('utf-8')` — matching the local branch's `encoding='utf-8'` (pipeline.py:279). If the reviewer wants GAP-020 strictly test-only, gate this single assertion behind an xfail referencing GAP-014; the preferred path is to make the one-line fix and assert parity (it is load-bearing for live news reads).
10. Run the verification command; confirm the new unit tests pass and the full suite stays green (77 -> 77+N unit tests).
11. Append a row to the Test Failure Mapping table in `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md` recording the command, result, and `GAP-020` (and `GAP-014` if the one-line fix is included), and flip the GAP-020 status note toward `closed` with the evidence.

**Files to touch:** `tests/test_pipeline_s3_readback.py (new — the deterministic s3/memory:// read-back tests)`  `src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py (one-line UTF-8 fix at the `_read_text` s3 branch, line 280, to enable Test 6 parity — this also closes GAP-014; omit only if scoping GAP-020 strictly test-only and xfailing Test 6)`  `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md (Test Failure Mapping row + GAP-020 status/evidence; note GAP-014 if fixed)`  `tests/fixtures/bronze/** (read-only reference for byte-for-byte parity in Test 4/5; do NOT modify — raw Bronze stays immutable)`

**Definition of Done (contract).**
- [ ] A new `tests/test_pipeline_s3_readback.py` exists, marked `pytest.mark.unit`, requiring no Docker/MinIO/network — it injects an fsspec `memory://` filesystem as `lander.s3`.
- [ ] Test asserts the `_list_bronze_files` s3 branch globs the seeded `bronze/<domain>/<source>/*/ingest_date=*/*` layout and `_is_data_file` excludes `.meta.json` sidecars.
- [ ] Test asserts the no-backend `ValueError` (`match='bronze_root or s3'`) for an object exposing neither `bronze_root` nor `s3`.
- [ ] Test asserts `_read_tsv` reads a gzip-over-s3 (`.tsv.gz`) object via the s3 branch and returns the correct DataFrame.
- [ ] Test asserts local/live read parity: identical bytes read via the Path branch (`bronze_root`) and the s3 branch (`memory://`) produce equal results for `_read_tsv` (assert_frame_equal) and for `_read_text`/`_read_bronze_news` (equal article dicts).
- [ ] A UTF-8 payload round-trips through the `_read_text` s3 branch regardless of OS locale (either via the GAP-014 one-line fix asserted green, or an explicit `xfail` referencing GAP-014 if test-only scope is chosen).
- [ ] Numeric/stat content read back is byte/value-identical to the source bytes — no LLM, no numeric rewriting anywhere in the test or fix.
- [ ] `python -m pytest -q -m unit` is green; total unit count increases from 77 with no regressions, and `python -m pytest -q` stays fully green.
- [ ] `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md` Test Failure Mapping has a new row with the exact command + result for GAP-020 (and GAP-014 if fixed), and the GAP-020 entry reflects the new evidence.

Seed the s3 side with in-memory copies via fs.pipe().", "fsspec MemoryFileSystem store is process-global and shared across tests — clear it at the start of each test (fs.store.clear()) or use unique paths to avoid leakage and flaky glob results.", "MemoryFileSystem.glob returns leading-slash str paths (e.g. `/bronze/...`); write with no leading slash (fs.pipe('bronze/...')) but expect glob results to be str (not Path) so they correctly take the s3 branch. ### GAP-021 — Make the Silver stats crosswalk cache re-attempt `unmapped` labels (no terminal-unmapped trap)

`MID` · level **silver** · effort **S** · depends on: none (self-contained Silver-layer fix; does not depend on infra/ollama-model since the LLM is stubbed in the test)

**Build:** Stop `build_crosswalk` from treating a cached `"unmapped"` value as final: re-attempt unmapped labels when the LLM later becomes available, and add a `force_rebuild` flag that ignores the cache, then prove it with a deterministic unit test.

**Context.** This is the Silver-layer LLM-assisted column crosswalk (`source_column` native-language stat label -> canonical English feature key). It sits between the deterministic Silver readers (which melt Bronze bytes into long frames) and `merge_sources` -> Gold pivot. The crosswalk is the only LLM touchpoint in the stats path; numbers never go through it. The cache (`silver/crosswalk_cache.json`, a review-and-commit artifact) is meant to make runs reproducible, but it currently poisons itself: a label resolved to `"unmapped"` during an Ollama-down / `use_llm=False` run is cached and never re-tried, so every later run replays the failure even with a working LLM. This blocks KSH/Statistik Austria/UIC HU/DE labels (the only labels that need the LLM) from ever mapping once a single offline run has committed `unmapped` for them. Severity is low because the active path (Eurostat/World Bank) maps by rule and never needs the LLM, but it is a correctness trap for the deferred `silver/stats-parsers-extra` work.

**Problem.** In `src/railway_lakehouse/silver/stats/merge.py`, `build_crosswalk` (lines 186-205) loads the cache (`_load_cache`, lines 112-118) and then at line 194-195 does `if label in cache: continue`. This skip is unconditional on the cached *value*: a cached `"unmapped"` is membership-present in the dict, so the label is skipped and never re-mapped. The only way a label gets a real key is on its very first encounter (line 197-200), where `_map_label_by_rule` (rule, no LLM) runs first and `_map_label_via_llm` (lines 127-140) runs only when `use_llm=True` and the source is one of `{None, "ksh", "statistik_austria", "uic"}`. So the failure mode is: run 1 with `use_llm=False` (Ollama down) caches `label -> "unmapped"` (line 200); run 2 with `use_llm=True` and a healthy stubbed/real LLM hits `if label in cache: continue` and the cached `"unmapped"` wins. There is also no escape hatch: no parameter forces recomputation, so even deleting-and-rebuilding requires manually editing the committed JSON. `_load_cache`/`_save_cache` always read/write `CROSSWALK_PATH`; there is no in-memory-only path. The existing test `tests/test_silver_characterization.py:40-55` only covers the happy first-pass rule mapping, not the re-attempt-after-unmapped behavior, so this gap is uncovered.

**Steps.**
1. Reproduce first: add the new test (RED). In tests/test_silver_characterization.py (module already has `pytestmark = pytest.mark.unit`), add a test that (a) monkeypatches `stats_merge.CROSSWALK_PATH` to `tmp_path/'crosswalk.json'`, (b) calls `build_crosswalk(['Vasuti aruszallitas (tonna-km)'], sources={'Vasuti aruszallitas (tonna-km)': 'ksh'}, use_llm=False)` and asserts the label cached as 'unmapped', (c) monkeypatches `stats_merge._map_label_via_llm` (or `stats_merge.generate_json`) to return a valid canonical key e.g. 'rail_freight_tonne_km', (d) re-runs `build_crosswalk([...], sources={...}, use_llm=True)` and asserts the label NOW maps to that key. Run `python -m pytest -q tests/test_silver_characterization.py -k crosswalk` and confirm the re-attempt assertion FAILS against current code (proves the bug).
2. Decide the contract (keep it minimal and non-breaking): keep `build_crosswalk(labels, *, sources=None, use_llm=True)` signature and ADD a keyword-only `force_rebuild: bool = False`. Re-attempt semantics: a label whose *cached value is a real canonical key* is still skipped (stable/reproducible); a label whose cached value is `'unmapped'` is re-attempted whenever the current call could plausibly do better — i.e. when `use_llm=True` (an LLM is now available that was not before) OR a rule now matches. When `force_rebuild=True`, ignore the existing cache entirely (start from `{}`) and recompute every label.
3. Fix `build_crosswalk` (merge.py:186-205). Replace the cache load with: `cache = {} if force_rebuild else _load_cache()`. Replace the loop body's skip guard so a real mapped key short-circuits but `'unmapped'` does not block re-attempt: `cached = cache.get(label)` ; `if cached is not None and cached != 'unmapped': continue`. Then run the existing rule-first + conditional-LLM block exactly as today. Guard against pointlessly overwriting an existing `'unmapped'` with `'unmapped'` (no behavior change, just clarity): only write `cache[label] = key or 'unmapped'` after attempting. Keep `_save_cache(cache)` and the existing INFO log line. Do NOT change the rule tables, `_map_label_via_llm`, or `merge_sources`.
4. Add a deterministic re-attempt path that does not require an LLM either, so the fix is provable without Ollama: ensure that if a label was cached `'unmapped'` and a NEW rule now matches (`_map_label_by_rule` returns non-None), it is upgraded on rerun even with `use_llm=False`. This falls out naturally from step 3 (the skip no longer fires for `'unmapped'`), but add an assertion for it in the test to lock it in.
5. Wire `force_rebuild` through callers WITHOUT changing their defaults (no behavior change): `pipeline.py:122`, `silver/run.py:38-39`, and `silver/stats/load.py:126-127` all call `build_crosswalk(...)`. Leave them as-is (they get `force_rebuild=False` by default). Optionally expose it on `pipeline.py` CLI as `--rebuild-crosswalk` (store_true) threaded into the `build_crosswalk` call and `build_silver_stats(use_llm=..., force_rebuild=...)`; if you add the CLI flag, also add `force_rebuild: bool = False` to `build_silver_stats` (load.py:114) and pass it through. This CLI flag is optional polish — the core DoD does not require it.
6. Update the docstring of `build_crosswalk` (lines 188-190) to state: cached real keys are stable; cached `'unmapped'` is re-attempted on later runs (e.g. once the LLM is reachable) and a rule match upgrades it; `force_rebuild=True` ignores the cache. Also update the module docstring bullet (lines 8-13) if it implies unmapped is terminal (it implies caching 'for review' — clarify it is re-attemptable).
7. Run the full deterministic suite (`python -m pytest -q`) and the unit marker (`python -m pytest -q -m unit`) to confirm GREEN and that the existing `test_build_crosswalk_maps_english_labels_by_rule_without_llm` still passes (the happy first-pass path must be unchanged). Run `python -m compileall -q src tests` and `git diff --check`.
8. Record the closure in docs/GAP_REGISTER.md: flip GAP-021 status to `closed` (or note evidence) and add a row to the Test Failure Mapping table with the exact verification command and result (e.g. `python -m pytest -q tests/test_silver_characterization.py -k crosswalk` -> passed). Update `.planning/COURSEWORK_PROGRESS.md`.

**Files to touch:** `C:\Users\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\Documents\tmp\ai-masters\coursework\bigdata\course_proj\src\railway_lakehouse\silver\stats\merge.py`  `C:\Users\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\Documents\tmp\ai-masters\coursework\bigdata\course_proj\tests\test_silver_characterization.py`  `C:\Users\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\Documents\tmp\ai-masters\coursework\bigdata\course_proj\docs\GAP_REGISTER.md`  `C:\Users\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\Documents\tmp\ai-masters\coursework\bigdata\course_proj\src\railway_lakehouse\silver\stats\load.py (optional, only if adding force_rebuild passthrough)`  `C:\Users\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\Documents\tmp\ai-masters\coursework\bigdata\course_proj\src\railway_lakehouse\pipeline.py (optional, only if adding --rebuild-crosswalk CLI flag)`

**Definition of Done (contract).**
- [ ] `build_crosswalk` no longer skips a label whose cached value is `'unmapped'`: a label cached `'unmapped'` (e.g. from a `use_llm=False` run) is re-attempted on a later `build_crosswalk(use_llm=True)` call and maps to the correct canonical key when the (stubbed) LLM returns one.
- [ ] A label cached as a real canonical key is NOT re-attempted (stays stable across reruns) — reproducibility is preserved.
- [ ] A `force_rebuild=True` keyword-only flag exists on `build_crosswalk` and ignores any existing cache (recomputes every label from scratch).
- [ ] All existing callers (`pipeline.py:122`, `silver/run.py:38`, `silver/stats/load.py:126`) keep their current behavior by default (no signature break; `force_rebuild` defaults to False).
