### GAP-023 — Make Eurostat geo filtering explicit and logged (stop silently dropping aggregate geos)

`MID` · level **silver** · effort **S** · depends on: none (independent of GAP-013/GAP-015; can land standalone). GAP-013 (live Eurostat SDMX-header crosswalk miss) is a separate prerequisite for Eurostat actually reaching Gold, but is NOT required to close GAP-023.

**Build:** Replace the implicit `,([A-Z]{2})$` geo regex in `read_eurostat_tsv` with an explicit allowed-geo filter that logs how many non-target/aggregate geos (EU27_2020, EA19, ...) it drops, so the filtering is intentional and auditable instead of a silent NaN side effect.

**Context.** This is a Silver-layer correctness/observability fix in the rail lakehouse pipeline: web sources -> Bronze -> Silver -> Gold -> Spark -> report. `read_eurostat_tsv` (src/railway_lakehouse/silver/stats/merge.py) melts wide Eurostat TSV into the long StatFact contract (geo, year, value, unit, source_dataset, source_column) that feeds the Gold (geo, year) feature matrix. Today the geo column is derived by a regex that only matches a trailing 2-uppercase-letter code; every aggregate/multi-char geo (EU27_2020, EA19, EU28, etc.) silently becomes NaN, survives the merge unflagged, then vanishes at the Gold pivot. GAP-023 is a `low`-severity silver gap and is also flagged in TASKS.md Wave 4 as part of the eurostat->Gold mapping effort. It does not touch Bronze immutability or numeric merge determinism.

**Problem.** In `src/railway_lakehouse/silver/stats/merge.py:66`, `read_eurostat_tsv` derives geo with:

    long["geo"] = long[id_col].astype(str).str.extract(r",([A-Z]{2})$")[0]

This regex silently coerces any non-2-ASCII-letter trailing geo token to NaN. Reproduced locally: for dimension keys `['A,KM,HU','A,KM,AT','A,KM,EU27_2020','A,KM,EA19','A,PC,DE']` it yields `['HU','AT', NaN, NaN, 'DE']` (2 silent NaNs, no log line). The drop is then invisible all the way to Gold:
- `merge_sources` (merge.py:211-227) only drops rows where `feature == "unmapped"` (line 220) and never inspects or logs the geo column, so NaN-geo rows enter the unified StatFact table.
- `pivot_stats` -> `pivot_table(index=["geo","year"], ...)` in `src/railway_lakehouse/gold/build.py:53-62` silently drops NaN index rows (reproduced: 3 long rows with one None geo -> 2 wide rows). 

Net effect: aggregate geos are filtered out with zero observability, and the behavior is an accidental property of a regex rather than a stated contract. The `StatFact.geo` docstring (src/railway_lakehouse/silver/schema.py:9) even lists `EU27` as a valid example geo, so the regex is also stricter than the schema's stated intent. Note: per GAP-013 / STATE_AND_ROADMAP.md:304, the live Eurostat path currently feeds the SDMX dimension-key header as `source_column` so Eurostat rows are dropped at the crosswalk anyway; GAP-023 is independent and concerns the geo filter being implicit+unlogged in the reader itself, which is the unit under test.

**Steps.**
1. Read src/railway_lakehouse/silver/stats/merge.py:59-74 (read_eurostat_tsv) and confirm line 66 is the geo-extraction regex; read merge.py:211-227 (merge_sources) to confirm geo is never filtered/logged downstream; read gold/build.py:53-62 (pivot_stats) to confirm NaN-geo rows are dropped at the pivot.
2. Add an explicit allowed-geo set as a module-level constant in merge.py near the other config (e.g. after CANON_KEYS / _WORLD_BANK_ISO3_TO_GEO, around line 37). Make it the project's target geos plus any deliberately-kept national codes. Recommended: derive from the existing project scope (HU, AT, and the CZ already present in _WORLD_BANK_ISO3_TO_GEO) but keep it a single named set, e.g. `TARGET_GEOS = {"HU", "AT", "CZ", "DE"}` (DE is already exercised in existing tests). Add a short comment that this is the explicit Eurostat geo allow-list and that aggregate geos (EU27_2020, EA19, ...) are intentionally excluded. Do NOT hardcode anything dataset/column-specific beyond geo codes — this stays a generic geo allow-list.
3. In read_eurostat_tsv, keep extracting the raw trailing geo token but widen the capture so aggregate codes are visible rather than silently NaN. Change the extraction to capture the full last comma-delimited token (e.g. `long["geo_raw"] = long[id_col].astype(str).str.rsplit(",", n=1).str[-1].str.strip()`), so EU27_2020/EA19 are present as strings, not NaN. Handle the no-comma / single-token case by falling back to the whole id string.
4. Apply the explicit filter: compute a boolean mask `keep = long["geo_raw"].isin(TARGET_GEOS)`, set `long["geo"] = long["geo_raw"].where(keep)`, and count the dropped rows that had a real (non-null, non-empty) geo token but were not in TARGET_GEOS. Then drop the non-target rows from the returned frame so the long output only contains target geos (this preserves current Gold output exactly for HU/AT/DE while making the filter explicit).
5. Log the drop with the existing module logger (logger = logging.getLogger("silver.stats.merge"), merge.py:30). Emit a single INFO line that records the dataset_id, the number of rows dropped, and the distinct dropped geo tokens, e.g. logger.info("eurostat %s: dropped %d rows for %d non-target/aggregate geo(s): %s", dataset_id, n_dropped, len(dropped_geos), sorted(dropped_geos)). Only log when n_dropped > 0 to avoid noise on clean fixtures.
6. Drop the temporary geo_raw helper column before returning, and ensure the returned frame still has exactly the documented columns: long[["geo", "year", "value", "unit", "source_dataset", "source_column"]] (merge.py:74). Do not change the numeric value parsing (lines 69-70) or the unit/source_column/source_dataset assignment — only the geo derivation + filtering.
7. Add a deterministic unit test in tests/test_silver_characterization.py (module is already @pytest.mark.unit at line 11, imports stats_merge at line 7). Construct a small wide Eurostat-style DataFrame whose id column mixes target geos and aggregates (e.g. id values 'A,KM,HU', 'A,KM,AT', 'A,KM,EU27_2020', 'A,KM,EA19'), call stats_merge.read_eurostat_tsv(df, "rail_demo"), and assert: (a) returned geos are exactly {HU, AT}; (b) no row has geo EU27_2020 or EA19; (c) the aggregate rows are absent (len of EU27_2020/EA19 subset == 0). Use caplog (pytest's built-in) at INFO level on logger name 'silver.stats.merge' to assert a drop-count line was emitted mentioning the number of dropped geos / the aggregate codes. Use only inline fixtures (no coursework/ data, no tmp_path needed since the reader writes nothing).
8. Run the verification command and confirm green; then update the GAP-023 row in docs/GAP_REGISTER.md status to reflect closure (status -> closed, add Evidence line citing the new test name and the passing command) ONLY after the command passes.
9. Optionally extend docs/DATA_CONTRACTS.md Silver Stats Contract (around line 30-45) with one sentence stating Eurostat geo selection uses an explicit allowed-geo set and that aggregate geos are excluded with a logged drop count — keep it short; this is a docs nicety, the code+test is the contract.

**Files to touch:** `src/railway_lakehouse/silver/stats/merge.py`  `tests/test_silver_characterization.py`  `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md`  `docs/DATA_CONTRACTS.md`

**Definition of Done (contract).**
- [ ] read_eurostat_tsv no longer uses the implicit `,([A-Z]{2})$` regex; geo selection goes through a single named, explicit allowed-geo set (TARGET_GEOS) defined as a module constant.
- [ ] When at least one row is filtered for a non-target/aggregate geo, read_eurostat_tsv emits exactly one INFO log line via logger 'silver.stats.merge' recording the dataset_id, the dropped-row count, and the distinct dropped geo tokens.

### GAP-025 — Make Silver RSS parsing fault-tolerant: skip + log malformed feeds instead of aborting the whole news batch

`MID` · level **silver** · effort **S** · depends on: none

**Build:** Wrap the XML parse in parse_rss_xml so a malformed RSS document is logged and skipped (returns []) instead of raising an unhandled xml.etree.ElementTree.ParseError that aborts the entire Silver news ingestion loop.

**Context.** Silver news ingestion reads many Bronze RSS/GDELT feed files in one pass and turns them into ArticleRecord rows that feed the LLM extractor and Gold news features. RSS feeds are externally sourced and routinely arrive truncated or non-well-formed (partial download, HTML error page served with a .xml name, encoding garble). Today a single bad feed kills the whole batch, so one flaky source silently zeroes out all news for a run. This is the GAP-025 robustness item (low severity, Wave 5 in docs/TASKS.md) and is purely defensive — it must not change parsing behavior for well-formed feeds.

**Problem.** src/railway_lakehouse/silver/news/rss.py:8-9 — parse_rss_xml(xml_text, source) calls `root = ET.fromstring(xml_text)` with no error handling. `xml.etree.ElementTree.fromstring` raises `xml.etree.ElementTree.ParseError` on any non-well-formed document, and that exception propagates uncaught.\n\nThe batch boundary is the pipeline news loop in src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py:213-237 (`_read_bronze_news`). It iterates over ALL Bronze news files (`_list_bronze_files(..., domain=\"news\", ...)`), and for each `.xml` path calls `_rss_article_records(text, source)` at pipeline.py:244-245, which is `[record.to_row() for record in parse_rss_xml(xml_text, source=source)]`. There is no try/except anywhere in that loop (pipeline.py:218-237). So a ParseError from one malformed feed propagates out of `_rss_article_records` → out of the `for path in ...` loop → out of `_read_bronze_news`, aborting ingestion of every other (valid) feed in the batch and any GDELT JSON files too. This is exactly the GAP-025 failure: \"one malformed feed aborts the entire Silver news batch.\"\n\nThe module currently does not import or use `logging` (rss.py:1-4 imports only `xml.etree.ElementTree`, `ArticleRecord`, and the two local helpers). The sibling module src/railway_lakehouse/silver/news/extract.py:14,21 establishes the project convention: `import logging` then `logger = logging.getLogger(\"silver.news.<module>\")` and `logger.warning(...)` for per-item degradation (see extract.py:77, extract_batch summary at extract.py:112).

**Steps.**
1. Read src/railway_lakehouse/silver/news/rss.py (whole file, 48 lines) and src/railway_lakehouse/silver/news/extract.py:14-21 to match the existing logging convention exactly: `import logging` at top, module-level `logger = logging.getLogger("silver.news.rss")`.
2. Edit rss.py: add `import logging` to the imports block (rss.py:1) and a module-level `logger = logging.getLogger("silver.news.rss")` after the imports (before the function).
3. Edit parse_rss_xml (rss.py:8-44): wrap the `root = ET.fromstring(xml_text)` call in a try/except catching `ET.ParseError`. On ParseError, call `logger.warning("skipping malformed RSS feed source=%s: %s", source, exc)` and `return []`. Per the repo Hard Rule on no silent failures, the warning must carry the source identifier and the exception detail; do NOT bare-`except` (only catch ET.ParseError so genuine programming errors still surface). Keep the existing well-formed-path logic (the for-loop over `.//item`, id assignment, ArticleRecord construction) byte-for-byte unchanged.
4. Do NOT change pipeline.py. The fix belongs in parse_rss_xml so both the pipeline caller (pipeline.py:245) and the direct Silver caller (rss_records_to_news_features, rss.py:47) inherit fault tolerance. Returning [] for a bad feed means the pipeline loop at pipeline.py:230-237 simply contributes zero articles for that file and continues to the next — no abort.
5. Add a deterministic unit test to tests/test_silver_news_parsers.py (this file already holds all parse_rss_xml tests and is marked `pytestmark = pytest.mark.unit` at line 7). Add `test_parse_rss_xml_skips_malformed_feed_without_raising`: call parse_rss_xml on a clearly malformed document (e.g. "<rss><channel><item><title>broken" — an unclosed tag) and assert it returns `[]` and does NOT raise. Use pytest's `caplog` fixture to assert a warning is logged (e.g. `assert any("malformed" in r.message.lower() or r.levelname == "WARNING" for r in caplog.records)` after `caplog.set_level(logging.WARNING, logger="silver.news.rss")`).
6. Add a second deterministic unit test that proves the batch-survival contract at the parse layer: `test_parse_rss_xml_valid_feed_unaffected_by_a_separate_bad_feed` — parse a malformed doc (asserting []), then parse a valid one-item doc (reuse the XML shape from test_parse_rss_xml_returns_article_records at lines 11-22) and assert the valid feed still yields its 1 ArticleRecord with the expected title/url. This demonstrates that a bad feed does not poison subsequent valid feeds.
7. Run the verification command and confirm green. Do not add an integration test for this gap — the failure mode is fully reproducible at the unit (parse-function) level and the closure criterion in GAP_REGISTER.md explicitly scopes it to `pytest -q -m unit`.

**Files to touch:** `C:\Users\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\Documents\tmp\ai-masters\coursework\bigdata\course_proj\src\railway_lakehouse\silver\news\rss.py`  `C:\Users\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\Documents\tmp\ai-masters\coursework\bigdata\course_proj\tests\test_silver_news_parsers.py`

**Definition of Done (contract).**
- [ ] parse_rss_xml in src/railway_lakehouse/silver/news/rss.py catches xml.etree.ElementTree.ParseError, logs a WARNING via a module-level `logging.getLogger("silver.news.rss")` that includes the `source` and the exception, and returns [] for a malformed document.
- [ ] A malformed feed no longer raises out of parse_rss_xml, so the pipeline news loop (pipeline.py:218-237) cannot be aborted by one bad RSS file.
- [ ] Well-formed RSS parsing is byte-for-byte unchanged: all existing tests in tests/test_silver_news_parsers.py (test_parse_rss_xml_returns_article_records, _prefers_full_content_over_description, _assigns_unique_ids_without_urls, _uses_existing_extraction) still pass unchanged.

- [ ] A new deterministic unit test asserts that after a malformed feed is skipped, a separate valid feed still parses to its expected ArticleRecord(s) — proving batch survival at the parse layer.

- [ ] `python -m pytest -q -m unit` is green; `python -m compileall -q src tests` is clean.

**Pitfalls.** "Do NOT add a bare `except Exception` — catch only `xml.etree.ElementTree.ParseError` (alias `ET.ParseError`) so real bugs still surface; the repo Hard Rule is 'no silent failures: catch -> log full details -> re-raise OR explicitly degrade', and here the explicit degradation (skip+log+return []) is the intended contract, not a swallow. The GDELT sibling parse_gdelt_artlist_json (gdelt.py:11, `json.loads`) has the analogous fragility but is OUT OF SCOPE for GAP-025 (json.JSONDecodeError is a separate, undocumented gap) — keep this PR surgical to RSS/ParseError so the closure criterion maps 1:1. Note ET.fromstring also raises ParseError on empty string and on HTML-served-as-XML, so the single except clause covers the realistic Bronze failure shapes. caplog asserts: pin the logger name in `caplog.set_level(logging.WARNING, logger=\"silver.news.rss\")` so the assertion is deterministic regardless of root logger config (basicConfig is set in pipeline.py:40 but not during isolated unit runs)."


## LOW

### GAP-022 — Robust, observable Gold news date parsing (mixed-format + RFC-822 RSS)

`LOW` · level **gold** · effort **S** · depends on: none (GAP-022 is self-contained robustness work; does not require GAP-007 Gold-from-Silver wiring, MinIO, or Ollama)

**Build:** Replace pandas single-format date inference in Gold news aggregation with a robust mixed-format parser that handles ISO, GDELT-compact, and RFC-822 dates, counts every valid-date row, and logs a warning for any present-but-unparseable date; also fix the pipeline's RFC-822-dropping date normalizer.

**Context.** Gold's aggregate_news derives the `year` dimension from each news row's `published_date`; that year is the join key onto the stats matrix, so a silently-dropped date means a silently-dropped news row in the final ML matrix. This sits at the Silver-news -> Gold boundary (src/railway_lakehouse/gold/build.py and src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py). The bug surfaces whenever a non-pipeline Silver path feeds Gold: silver/persist.py stores NewsFeature.published_date verbatim as a string (RSS pubDate is RFC-822, GDELT seendate is compact YYYYMMDDTHHMMSSZ, others ISO), and gold/run.py:build_from_silver reads it back via load_news straight into aggregate_news, bypassing the pipeline's _normalize_article_date. GAP-022 is low severity, on the robustness track (Wave 5 in docs/TASKS.md).

**Problem.** Two confirmed defects, both reproduced empirically on pandas 3.0.3.

(1) src/railway_lakehouse/gold/build.py:74 — `_news_to_df` does `pd.to_datetime(df.get("published_date"), errors="coerce").dt.year.astype("Int64")`. With errors="coerce" and no `format`, pandas infers ONE format from the first non-null element and coerces every other format to NaT WITHOUT warning. Reproduced: pd.to_datetime(["2020-04-01","20200401","Mon, 23 Jun 2026 14:30:00 +0200"], errors="coerce") -> years [2020, NaN, NaN], no warning. Those NaT rows are then dropped by `df["year"].notna()` at gold/build.py:86, so mixed-format Silver news silently loses rows in Gold with zero observability.

(2) src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py:342-357 — `_normalize_article_date` concatenates ALL digits of the input then slices, which mishandles RFC-822 RSS dates (the format parse_rss_xml at silver/news/rss.py:8-16 stores verbatim from <pubDate>). Reproduced: "Tue, 01 Apr 2020 00:00:00 GMT" -> digits "012020000000" (12) -> 8-branch slices "01202000" -> %Y%m%d -> NaT -> returns None (dropped). Worse, "Wed, 02 Oct 2002 15:00:00 +0200" -> digits "0220021500000200" (16) -> 14-branch slices "02200215000002" -> %Y%m%d%H%M%S -> "0220-02-15" (year 220!), a silently CORRUPTED date, not a drop. A proper parser pd.to_datetime(text, utc=True) yields 2020-04-01 and 2002-10-02 respectively. So RSS dates are either dropped or corrupted in the live pipeline path.

Net effect: the GAP register only lists the RFC-822 drop, but the heuristic also corrupts some RFC-822 dates. Both the Gold inference bug (path-independent) and the pipeline normalizer bug (RSS-specific) must be fixed.

**Steps.**
1. Reproduce first (no edits). Run the two snippets from the Problem section in a python -c to see [2020, NaN, NaN] from the Gold path and None/0220-02-15 from _normalize_article_date. Confirm gold/build.py:74 and pipeline.py:342-357 are the exact lines.
2. Add a shared date helper. Create src/railway_lakehouse/silver/news/dates.py with a pure function `parse_published_to_year(values: pd.Series) -> pd.Series` returning Int64 years, plus `normalize_published_date(value) -> str | None` returning an ISO date. Implement a deterministic two-pass parse: Pass 1 `pd.to_datetime(s, errors='coerce', utc=True, format='mixed')` (handles ISO and RFC-822, absorbing tz with utc=True); Pass 2 for still-NaT-but-present values, strip non-digits and try `%Y%m%d%H%M%S` on the first 14 digits then `%Y%m%d` on the first 8 (rescues GDELT-compact YYYYMMDDTHHMMSSZ and bare YYYYMMDD). This is fully deterministic and does NOT use an LLM. Verified working: ISO/bare/GDELT-compact/two RFC-822 variants all parse; only genuine garbage stays NaT.
3. Make Gold observable. In src/railway_lakehouse/gold/build.py, import the helper and rewrite _news_to_df (line 74) to: compute `parsed_year = parse_published_to_year(df.get('published_date'))`; identify present-but-unparseable rows (`raw.notna() & raw.astype(str).str.strip().ne('') & parsed_year.isna()`); if any, `logger.warning('aggregate_news: %d news rows have an unparseable published_date and are dropped: %r', n, sample)` using the module logger at gold/build.py:26; assign df['year'] = parsed_year. Do NOT change the downstream notna() filter at line 86 (genuinely undated rows stay dropped, by design).
4. Fix the pipeline normalizer. In src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py, replace the body of _normalize_article_date (lines 342-357) to delegate to silver.news.dates.normalize_published_date so RFC-822 RSS dates parse to a correct ISO date instead of being dropped/corrupted. Keep the exact None-on-empty / None-on-unparseable contract that test_pipeline_article_normalization_handles_missing_body_dates_and_fallback_ids (tests/test_pipeline_gaps.py:140) and the fixture e2e test depend on. Verify the existing assertion 'April 1, 2020' -> '2020-04-01' and '2020-04-01' -> '2020-04-01' still hold; add GDELT-compact handling so '20200401T120000Z' -> '2020-04-01' is preserved (currently relied on by test_pipeline_bronze_readers_load_local_fixtures, tests/test_pipeline_gaps.py:27-36).
5. Add the deterministic test (the DoD test). Append to tests/test_gold_characterization.py (module already has `pytestmark = pytest.mark.unit`) a test `test_aggregate_news_counts_mixed_format_dates_and_warns_on_unparseable` that builds dict news rows (same shape as the existing test_aggregate_news_* fixtures at lines 63-108) with three rail-related HU/AT rows whose published_date are ISO ('2020-04-01'), GDELT-compact ('20200615T120000Z') and RFC-822 ('Wed, 02 Oct 2002 15:00:00 +0200'), plus one rail-related row with an unparseable-but-present date ('not-a-date'). Assert: every valid-date row is counted (sum of news_article_count across the resulting (geo,year) groups equals 3, and the 2002/2020 years appear), AND that a warning is logged for the unparseable row (use pytest `caplog.at_level(logging.WARNING, logger='gold.build')` and assert the message mentions unparseable). Use only in-test fixtures; no coursework/ data, no tmp_path needed (pure in-memory).
6. Add a focused normalizer test. In tests/test_pipeline_gaps.py (module is `pytest.mark.integration`) OR better in a unit-marked test, assert pipeline._normalize_article_date('Tue, 01 Apr 2020 00:00:00 GMT') == '2020-04-01' and that the previously-corrupting 'Wed, 02 Oct 2002 15:00:00 +0200' == '2002-10-02' (regression guard against the year-220 corruption). Keep '20200401T120000Z' -> '2020-04-01' and '' / None -> None.
7. Run the full suite and the targeted unit subset; confirm no regression in the 87 existing tests. Update the Test Failure Mapping table in docs/GAP_REGISTER.md with the passing command + evidence, and flip GAP-022 status to closed once verification passes.

**Files to touch:** `src/railway_lakehouse/silver/news/dates.py (new — shared deterministic date helper)`  `src/railway_lakehouse/gold/build.py (rewrite _news_to_df at line 74; import helper; warn on unparseable)`  `src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py (rewrite _normalize_article_date lines 342-357 to delegate to the helper)`  `tests/test_gold_characterization.py (add mixed-format + warning unit test)`  `tests/test_pipeline_gaps.py (add _normalize_article_date RFC-822 regression assertions)`  `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md (update Test Failure Mapping row + flip GAP-022 to closed)`

**Definition of Done (contract).**
- [ ] A new pure helper silver/news/dates.py parses ISO, bare YYYYMMDD, GDELT-compact YYYYMMDDTHHMMSSZ, and RFC-822 dates deterministically (no LLM) and returns NaT/None only for genuinely unparseable input.
- [ ] gold/build.py:_news_to_df uses the helper; every news row with a parseable published_date (any of the four formats) is counted in aggregate_news output and contributes to news_article_count.
- [ ] aggregate_news logs a WARNING via the 'gold.build' logger for rows whose published_date is present (non-empty) but unparseable; rows with None/empty published_date are still silently dropped (unchanged contract).
- [ ] pipeline._normalize_article_date returns the correct ISO date for RFC-822 inputs ('Tue, 01 Apr 2020 00:00:00 GMT' -> '2020-04-01') and no longer corrupts dates like 'Wed, 02 Oct 2002 15:00:00 +0200' (-> '2002-10-02', not '0220-02-15'); '20200401T120000Z' -> '2020-04-01' and ''/None -> None are preserved.
- [ ] A deterministic unit test in tests/test_gold_characterization.py feeds mixed-format published_date (ISO + GDELT-compact + RFC-822) through aggregate_news, asserts every valid-date row is counted, and asserts the warning fires for a present-but-unparseable date.
- [ ] A regression test guards _normalize_article_date against the RFC-822 drop and the year-220 corruption.
- [ ] All previously-passing tests still pass (87 before; >=89 after) with no new xfails; tests use only in-memory fixtures (no coursework/ data).
- [ ] docs/GAP_REGISTER.md Test Failure Mapping records the green command and GAP-022 is marked closed.

**Verify:** `From repo root (C:\\Users\\XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX\\Documents\\tmp\\ai-masters\\coursework\\bigdata\\course_proj): `python -m pytest -q -m unit` (the GAP-022 closure command per the register row) must pass including the new mixed-format/warning test. Also run the full suite to prove no regression: `python -m pytest -q` (expect all green, >=89 passed, 0 xfailed). Optional targeted run while iterating: `python -m pytest -q tests/test_gold_characterization.py tests/test_pipeline_gaps.py`.`

**Pitfalls.** Determinism / Hard Rules: the date parser must be pure and deterministic — NO LLM and no numeric rewriting of stats; this is news-date parsing only, raw Bronze is untouched. Do NOT change the notna() drop at gold/build.py:86 — genuinely undated rows must still be excluded (changing it would inject NaN years into the join key). Preserve the exact _normalize_article_date contract the existing tests assert: 'April 1, 2020' -> '2020-04-01' (tests/test_pipeline_gaps.py:156), '20200401T120000Z' -> '2020-04-01' (tests/test_pipeline_gaps.py:32-35), and ''/None -> None; breaking these breaks the fixture e2e integration test. Use utc=True in pd.to_datetime to absorb RFC-822 timezone offsets, but only the .date()/.year is kept downstream so tz does not leak into output. pandas 'format=mixed' emits no per-row warning on coercion — you must compute the unparseable mask yourself for the WARNING log, do not rely on a pandas warning. Keep year as Int64 (nullable) after parsing so the existing astype('Int64') and notna() semantics hold. Tests must not read coursework/ data — build news rows inline. The 'gold.build' logger name (gold/build.py:26) is what caplog must target. Note _news_to_df is reached both via the pipeline path (where dates are already ISO-normalized) and via gold/run.build_from_silver + silver/persist.load_news (where dates are still in native RSS/GDELT formats) — the fix at gold/build.py:74 is what makes Gold robust regardless of which Silver path fed it, so do not assume dates are pre-normalized.

### GAP-024 — Correct the Bronze lander/RSS "auditable accumulate" docstrings and DATA_CONTRACTS.md to state day-granularity replace, and pin the real behavior with a deterministic test

`LOW` · level **docs** · effort **S** · depends on: none (self-contained; no code dependency on other gaps). Note for sequencing: GAP-024 touches the same DATA_CONTRACTS.md Bronze section and the same docs/index.html open-gaps list as other low docs gaps (GAP-029, GAP-030) — coordinate merge order to avoid trivial doc merge conflicts, but there is no functional dependency.

**Build:** Make the Bronze lander docstring, the RSS source docstring, and DATA_CONTRACTS.md tell the truth — a same-day re-pull REPLACES the prior object and its .meta.json at day granularity (it does not accumulate) — and add a unit test that proves/pins that behavior so docs and code can never silently diverge again.

**Context.** Bronze is the immutable raw-landing layer (AGENTS.md:74 Hard Rule: "Keep raw web data immutable in Bronze"). The RawLander is the only writer to the Bronze bucket and its provenance sidecars (`<file>.meta.json`) are the audit trail the project leans on for the "yearly stats / weekly news online-update" requirement. GAP-024 is a low-severity correctness-of-documentation gap: the lander's own docstring promises re-pulls "ACCUMULATE as history instead of overwriting," but the path is keyed on `ingest_date=YYYY-MM-DD` (day granularity) with a fixed filename, so a second pull on the same UTC day silently overwrites both the raw object and its provenance meta. The Silver persisted-outputs contract was already corrected for exactly this (DATA_CONTRACTS.md:84-86 explicitly says each `ingest_date` partition is "one replaceable snapshot"); the Bronze contract and docstrings were left stating the opposite. This sits at the very front of the pipeline (Bronze landing), so a misleading audit guarantee here undermines provenance claims in the report.

**Problem.** The claim and the code contradict each other:
- `src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/lander.py:6-9` (module docstring) asserts: "each pull lands under ingest_date=YYYY-MM-DD, so re-pulls ACCUMULATE as history instead of overwriting -- this is what makes the yearly (stats) and weekly (news) online-update requirements auditable."
- But `RawLander._partition_prefix` (`lander.py:56-60`) builds the prefix from `ingest_date` only, and `RawLander.land` (`lander.py:62-67`) sets `obj_path = f"{prefix}/{a.filename}"` and `meta_path = f"{obj_path}.meta.json"` with a fixed filename. The writes at `lander.py:86-89` use `s3.open(obj_path, "wb")` / `s3.open(meta_path, "w")` — both truncating opens. A same-day re-pull of the same `(domain, source, dataset_id, filename)` writes to the identical path and overwrites the prior raw bytes AND the prior `.meta.json` provenance (sha256, byte_size, fetch_timestamp_utc, ingest_run_id). Re-pulls only "accumulate" across distinct UTC days, never within a day.
- The same false promise is repeated in the RSS source docstring `src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/sources/rss_media.py:7-8`: "Re-polls accumulate under ingest_date, so items that scroll off a feed between polls are still captured historically." Intra-day re-polls do not accumulate; they replace.
- `docs/DATA_CONTRACTS.md:23-28` ("Bronze path pattern") shows the `ingest_date=YYYY-MM-DD` layout but says nothing about same-day replace semantics, while the Silver section directly below (DATA_CONTRACTS.md:84-86) correctly states the replace rule for its own `ingest_date` partitions. The Bronze contract is the one place a reader checks for the audit guarantee, and it is silent/misleading.
- The local analogue `LocalBronzeLander.land` (`bronze/live_check.py:54-69`) has the same day-granularity path (`f"ingest_date={ingest_date}"` at line 63, fixed filename at 64) and the same `write_bytes`/`write_text` truncating writes (lines 69, 86). `run_live_check` de-conflicts at the run level by nesting output under a `run_id` dir (`_resolve_run_output_dir`, live_check.py:645-654), but the lander's own `land()` still replaces on a repeated same-run land of the same artifact — so the docstring fix and the test should reflect that the lander primitive replaces.

Net: a documented audit guarantee ("auditable accumulate, not overwrite") is false at day granularity, and nothing pins the real behavior, so the docs and code can silently drift again.

**Steps.**
1. Read the full picture first (already traced): lander.py:1-104, rss_media.py:1-49, live_check.py:45-99, DATA_CONTRACTS.md:1-98, AGENTS.md:72-81 (Hard Rules), pyproject.toml:37-47 (markers). Confirm the decision below before editing.
2. DECISION (recommended Option A — documentation correction; this is the register's intent and lowest blast radius): align the Bronze docstrings and DATA_CONTRACTS.md with the actual day-granularity REPLACE semantics, mirroring the wording already adopted for Silver at DATA_CONTRACTS.md:84-86. Do NOT change the on-disk path layout (Option B below) in this task — that would change semantics the pipeline Bronze readers and committed fixtures depend on. If the user explicitly wants genuine accumulation, see the Option B note in pitfalls and stop to get sign-off first.
3. Edit `src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/lander.py:4-13` (module docstring). Replace the false 'ACCUMULATE as history instead of overwriting' bullet with truthful day-granularity wording, e.g.: re-pulls partition by `ingest_date=YYYY-MM-DD`; a re-pull on a NEW day accumulates a new partition, but a same-day re-pull of the same `(domain, source, dataset_id, filename)` REPLACES that day's object and its `.meta.json` provenance (day-granularity snapshot, not append). State that to retain multiple same-day snapshots, partition by `ingest_run_id` (carried in meta and available as `self.run_id`) — matching the Silver contract note. Keep the 'bytes first, metadata second' invariant description intact.
4. Edit the `RawLander.land` docstring at `src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/lander.py:63` to one truthful line: writes raw bytes + sidecar metadata to the day partition; a same-day re-land of the same artifact replaces both. (Keep it short — the module docstring carries the full explanation.)
5. Edit `src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/sources/rss_media.py:7-8`. Replace 'Re-polls accumulate under ingest_date, so items that scroll off a feed between polls are still captured historically.' with truthful wording: re-polls on a new day accumulate a new daily snapshot; same-day re-polls replace that day's landed feed (day-granularity). Note that items scrolling off a feed are captured only across days, not within a day. Do not change any fetch/landing logic — docstring only.
6. Edit `src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/live_check.py` `LocalBronzeLander` docstring at line 46 ('Local writer with the same path semantics as the Bronze lander.') to add one clause making the day-granularity replace explicit, so the local analogue documents the same contract.
7. Edit `docs/DATA_CONTRACTS.md` Bronze section (after the path pattern block, around line 28). Add a short bullet list mirroring the Silver wording at DATA_CONTRACTS.md:84-86: each `ingest_date=YYYY-MM-DD` partition is one replaceable daily snapshot; re-pulling on a new day adds a new partition (accumulates across days); a same-day re-pull of the same `(domain, source, dataset_id, filename)` overwrites that day's object and its `.meta.json`; to retain multiple same-day snapshots, partition by `ingest_run_id`. Keep raw bytes immutable per the Hard Rule — this is about partition granularity, not mutating landed bytes.
8. Add a deterministic unit test pinning the real REPLACE behavior so docs and code cannot silently diverge again. Add it to `tests/test_bronze_live_check.py` (it already imports `LocalBronzeLander` and `RawArtifact`, uses `tmp_path`, an injectable `clock`, and `pytestmark = pytest.mark.unit`; the existing `test_local_lander_writes_raw_file_and_metadata_in_bronze_layout` at line 37 is the exact model). New test `test_local_lander_same_day_repull_replaces_object_and_meta`: construct a `LocalBronzeLander(tmp_path, run_id='run-001', clock=lambda: FIXED_NOW)`; land artifact v1 (content=b'<rss>v1</rss>'); land a v2 artifact with the SAME `(domain, source, dataset_id, filename)` but content=b'<rss>v2-longer</rss>' under the SAME fixed clock; assert the raw file now reads v2 bytes (replaced, not appended), assert there is exactly ONE file (no v2-suffixed sibling) in the `ingest_date=2026-06-21` partition dir, and assert the `.meta.json` now records v2's `byte_size` and `sha256` (provenance overwritten). This documents 'same-day re-pull replaces object and provenance' as an executed fact backing the docstring/contract wording.
9. (Optional, strengthens the contract) Also assert the cross-day case is accumulate: land v1 under FIXED_NOW (2026-06-21) and v3 under a clock returning 2026-06-22, then assert TWO `ingest_date=` partition dirs exist with their respective bytes — proving 'accumulates across days, replaces within a day'.
10. Dashboard sync (Hard Rule AGENTS.md:81, enforced by the dashboard-sync-reminder bot since this touches `src/railway_lakehouse/**` and `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md`): update `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md` GAP-024 row (line 52) Status open->closed with a dated closure note citing the docstring/contract edits and the new test; flip the GAP-024 chip in `docs/index.html` (line 334) out of the open-gaps list (or mark resolved per the file's convention); update `docs/TASKS.md` if it tracks a matching task; add a Test Failure Mapping row in GAP_REGISTER.md for the new pytest command; append a handoff entry to `docs/PROGRESS_LOG.md`.
11. Run the verification command(s) and record results.

### GAP-026 — Make gold.aggregate_news honor its dict-or-object input contract (no KeyError on partial dict news rows)

`LOW` · level **gold** · effort **S** · depends on: none

**Build:** Default the optional NewsFeature fields inside _news_to_df so aggregate_news aggregates partial dict rows instead of raising an opaque pandas KeyError.

**Context.** aggregate_news is the deterministic Gold stage that turns per-article NewsFeature rows into the per-(geo, year) news_* feature block that joins onto the stats matrix (gold/build.py:78-121, called from build_gold at build.py:132). Its docstring and signature advertise a "dict-or-object" input contract (build.py:8 "a list of NewsFeature (or their dicts)", build.py:71 branches on isinstance(r, dict)), but only the object branch (NewsFeature.to_row()/asdict) is guaranteed to carry every field. A hand-built dict that omits optional fields — exactly what an external caller, a future non-pipeline Silver path, or a test would supply — crashes deep in pandas. This is a robustness/contract gap on the active news-to-Gold path (Stage 2, GAP-006/GAP-016 neighborhood), low severity, scheduled in re-audit Wave 5 alongside the other Gold robustness fixes.

**Problem.** aggregate_news raises an opaque pandas KeyError when a dict news row omits optional NewsFeature fields, contradicting the advertised dict-or-object contract. The rows are funneled through _news_to_df (src/railway_lakehouse/gold/build.py:68-75): line 71 `rows = [r if isinstance(r, dict) else r.to_row() for r in news_rows]` passes dicts straight through, line 72 `df = pd.DataFrame(rows)` so the DataFrame only has columns the dicts happened to include. Reproduced on a clean checkout — feeding `[{'article_id':'n1','country':'HU','published_date':'2020-04-01','is_rail_related':True,'event_type':'investment','sentiment':'positive'}]` (omitting monetary_amount_eur and operators) raises `KeyError "Label(s) ['monetary_amount_eur'] do not exist"` at build.py:92 (the `grp.agg(...)` block, build.py:92-97). Peeling that field back reveals the failure cascade across every column access that does NOT use .get: (1) build.py:84 `df["country"].isin(...)` -> KeyError 'country'; (2) build.py:89 `df["sentiment"].map(...)` -> KeyError 'sentiment'; (3) build.py:96 `news_total_investment_eur=("monetary_amount_eur","sum")` -> KeyError on monetary_amount_eur; (4) build.py:108 `df[["country","year","operators"]]` -> KeyError "['operators'] not in index"; (5) build.py:101 `pivot_table(..., columns="event_type", ...)` -> KeyError 'event_type' when that column is entirely absent. (is_rail_related at build.py:84 already uses df.get so it is the one safe access — a missing is_rail_related silently filters all rows out rather than crashing, which is also undesirable but not a crash.) The GAP register names only monetary_amount_eur/operators (build.py:71,96,108) but the reproduced cascade proves country, sentiment, and event_type must also be defaulted for the contract to actually hold.

**Steps.**
1. Read src/railway_lakehouse/gold/build.py:68-121 and src/railway_lakehouse/silver/schema.py:38-58 (NewsFeature) together: the canonical set of columns aggregate_news consumes is article_id, published_date, is_rail_related, country, event_type, sentiment, monetary_amount_eur, operators. NewsFeature.to_row() (asdict) always emits all of them; a partial dict may omit any.
2. Fix at the single funnel — _news_to_df (build.py:68-75) — so both dict and object inputs reach aggregate_news with a uniform, fully-populated schema. After building `df = pd.DataFrame(rows)` (build.py:72) and before the existing year-derivation line (build.py:74), reindex/default the consumed columns deterministically with type-appropriate defaults: scalar object/string columns (country, event_type, sentiment) default to None; is_rail_related defaults to False; monetary_amount_eur defaults to None (NOT 0 — preserve the existing sum semantics where absent money does not inflate news_total_investment_eur); operators defaults to an empty list per row.
3. Concretely: build a small list of expected scalar columns and assign each missing one via `if col not in df.columns: df[col] = default`. For operators, because a column-level default must be a list-per-row (not a shared mutable list), populate it with `df['operators'] = [[] for _ in range(len(df))]` only when the column is absent; when present, leave the caller's lists untouched. Guard the empty-DataFrame case: _news_to_df already returns an empty df early at build.py:69-70 when news_rows is falsy, but pd.DataFrame(rows) on non-empty rows that are all empty dicts is still non-empty — keep the column-defaulting logic running on any non-empty df so downstream column access is safe.
4. Keep is_rail_related handling consistent: now that the column always exists, the filter at build.py:84 can stay as `df.get('is_rail_related') == True` or be tightened to `df['is_rail_related'] == True`; either works once the column is guaranteed. Do not change the filter semantics (still only rows with is_rail_related truthy AND country in {HU, AT} AND a parseable year are counted).
5. Do NOT alter the aggregation math, the source-priority/conflict logic, the pivot/rename to news_n_<event> / news_op_<op>, or any numeric value — this is purely about column presence with safe defaults. No LLM, no numeric rewriting (Hard Rule).
6. Add a deterministic unit test in tests/test_gold_characterization.py (it already exists, pytestmark = pytest.mark.unit at line 7, imports gold.build as gold_build). Add test_aggregate_news_handles_partial_dict_rows that passes a dict omitting monetary_amount_eur and operators (the GAP-named minimum) and asserts aggregate_news returns without raising and applies defaults (e.g. news_total_investment_eur == 0.0 because the only article had no money, news_article_count == 1). Add a second assertion-rich case (or extend the test) covering a row that ALSO omits country/sentiment/event_type to lock in the full cascade fix — assert no raise and that a row missing country is excluded (since country must be HU/AT), and that a row with country=HU but missing event_type/sentiment/monetary still aggregates (news_article_count counted, news_sentiment_mean NaN, money summing to 0).
7. Run the exact verification command and confirm green; also run the full unit marker to confirm the existing test_aggregate_news_counts_events_sentiment_money_and_operators (build.py test:63-108) and test_build_gold_fills_count_like_news_columns_with_zero (test:111-130) still pass unchanged.

**Files to touch:** `src/railway_lakehouse/gold/build.py`  `tests/test_gold_characterization.py`

**Definition of Done (contract).**
- [ ] aggregate_news([{dict omitting monetary_amount_eur and operators}]) returns a DataFrame without raising (defaults applied) — the exact GAP-026 closure criterion.
- [ ] The full reproduced cascade is fixed: dict rows omitting any of country, sentiment, monetary_amount_eur, operators, or event_type no longer raise KeyError in aggregate_news.
- [ ] monetary_amount_eur defaults to None/absent-as-0 in the sum (an article with no money contributes 0 to news_total_investment_eur, not a spurious value); operators defaults to an empty list (contributes no operator counts).
- [ ] The fix lives in _news_to_df (the single dict-or-object funnel, build.py:68-75); aggregation math, conflict resolution, pivots, renames, and all numeric values are unchanged (Hard Rule: deterministic, no LLM numeric rewriting).
- [ ] Existing tests test_aggregate_news_counts_events_sentiment_money_and_operators and test_build_gold_fills_count_like_news_columns_with_zero still pass unchanged (no regression to the full-dict path).
- [ ] A new deterministic unit test in tests/test_gold_characterization.py covers the partial-dict contract, uses no coursework/ data (inline dict fixtures only), and is collected under the unit marker.
- [ ] The new test and the full unit suite pass via the verification command.

**Verify:** `python -m pytest -q -m unit (and, to scope the new test directly: python -m pytest -q tests/test_gold_characterization.py)`

**Pitfalls.** "Do not default monetary_amount_eur to 0 — that would inflate news_total_investment_eur and silently rewrite a numeric Gold feature (violates the deterministic-stats Hard Rule and breaks the absent-money semantics); use None so the pandas sum treats it as absent. Operators must be defaulted as a fresh per-row empty list ([[] for _ in range(len(df))]), never a single shared list object assigned to the column, to avoid aliasing/mutation bugs and pandas broadcasting a list into every cell incorrectly. Fix only in _news_to_df, not by sprinkling .get all over aggregate_news — the funnel is the contract boundary. The GAP register text names only monetary_amount_eur/operators, but the verified cascade requires also defaulting country, sentiment, and event_type; defaulting just the two named fields will still crash on the others, so the test must cover the full set. Do not change the is_rail_related filter semantics or the HU/AT country filter. Keep the early empty-news return (build.py:69-70). This is a Gold-layer in-memory change only — it does not touch raw Bronze (immutable) and writes nothing under output/. Tests must use inline dict fixtures (tmp_path/generated), never coursework/ data."

### GAP-027 — MinIO default credentials & port exposure: document the local-only posture and allow override

`LOW` · level **ops** · effort **S** · depends on: none

**Build:** Make the insecure `admin`/`password123` MinIO defaults explicit and overridable, and (optionally) bind the published ports to loopback, so a teammate who runs the stack on a shared/lab host is not silently exposed.

**Context.** The local lakehouse store ships convenient defaults so `docker compose up -d` + `scripts/minio_smoke.py` work with zero config. That convenience is correct for local dev, but the defaults are well-known and the service is published on all interfaces with `restart: unless-stopped`, so on a shared or internet-reachable host it is an open MinIO with admin/admin-class creds. This is a docs/ops hardening note, not a pipeline bug.

**Problem.** `docker-compose.yml:20-21` sets `MINIO_ROOT_USER: ${S3_KEY:-admin}` / `MINIO_ROOT_PASSWORD: ${S3_SECRET:-password123}` (same fallbacks repeated at lines 34-35 for `createbuckets`); ports are published as `"9000:9000"` / `"9001:9001"` with no `127.0.0.1:` prefix (binds `0.0.0.0`). `README.md` echoes `admin` / `password123`. `src/railway_lakehouse/bronze/config.py` and `silver/config.py` default `S3_KEY`/`S3_SECRET` to the same values. There is no note that these are local-only and must be overridden for any non-loopback host.

**Steps.**
1. In `README.md` (the "Local lakehouse (MinIO)" section) add a short security note: `admin`/`password123` are **insecure local-only defaults**; set `S3_KEY`/`S3_SECRET` in `.env` for any shared, lab, or non-loopback host. State that the stack reads these from `.env` (already wired by `scripts/minio_smoke.py`'s `_load_dotenv`).
2. (Optional, recommended) In `docker-compose.yml` bind the ports to loopback — `"127.0.0.1:9000:9000"` / `"127.0.0.1:9001:9001"` — OR add a comment documenting the deliberate `0.0.0.0` exposure for LAN access. Pick one and say why.
3. Confirm `.env.example` shows `S3_KEY` / `S3_SECRET` so the override path is obvious (do not put real secrets in it — placeholders only).
4. Verify no real secret is committed anywhere (only variable names / placeholder dev defaults).

**Files to touch:** `README.md`  `docker-compose.yml`  `.env.example`

**Definition of Done (contract).**
- [ ] README's MinIO section documents `admin`/`password123` as insecure local-only defaults requiring an `.env` override for shared/non-loopback hosts.
- [ ] Either `docker-compose.yml` binds the MinIO ports to `127.0.0.1` **or** a comment documents the intentional `0.0.0.0` exposure and its trade-off.
- [ ] `.env.example` shows `S3_KEY` / `S3_SECRET` override keys (placeholders, not real secrets).
- [ ] `grep -ni password123 docker-compose.yml .env.example README.md` shows only documented local defaults — no real credentials anywhere in the repo.

**Verify:** `grep -ni "password123\|S3_KEY\|S3_SECRET" docker-compose.yml .env.example README.md` and manual review of the README MinIO section + compose port mappings.

**Pitfalls.** Keep the convenient local defaults working **without** an `.env` so the smoke script and `docker compose up -d` still run out-of-the-box (do not make creds mandatory). Never print or commit a real secret — variable names and the existing dev placeholders only. Docs/ops only: do not change pipeline code, Bronze immutability, or the smoke round-trip behavior.

### GAP-028 — Add a CI workflow that installs the package and runs the unit+integration test suite on PRs and pushes

`LOW` · level **ops** · effort **S** · depends on: none (the suite is already green; this only adds automation). Note: do NOT add the `[spark]` extra to CI — leaving it out sidesteps GAP-017 (unbounded `pyspark>=3.5` resolving to Spark 4.x). GAP-018 (lockfile/version bounds) is independent; CI here intentionally tests the floor interpreter (3.12) rather than pinning the full stack.

**Build:** Add `.github/workflows/ci.yml` that runs `pip install -e ".[test]"` then `pytest -q -m "unit or integration"` on every PR and push, so the deterministic test suite is enforced automatically and a green run is recorded.

**Context.** CI is the only ops gate missing from an otherwise test-heavy repo: there are 87 deterministic tests (`python -m pytest -q -m "unit or integration"` → 87 passed in ~2.2s, no network/Docker), but nothing runs them automatically. The sole GitHub Actions workflow (`.github/workflows/dashboard-sync-reminder.yml`) is a non-blocking comment bot that never executes the suite. This sits at the ops/DevEx layer: it protects every other gap's "verification command" (e.g. GAP-012..030 closure criteria all run pytest) by making regressions visible on PRs to the shared `pol3et/railway-bigdata` repo. It is severity `low` because contributors can still run pytest by hand, but it is cheap, high-leverage insurance for a multi-contributor coursework repo.

**Problem.** No workflow runs the test suite. `.github/workflows/` contains exactly one file, `dashboard-sync-reminder.yml`, which (lines 9-11, 22) triggers on `pull_request_target` and only runs `actions/github-script@v7` to post a dashboard-sync comment — it never checks out PR code or runs pytest (the header comment at lines 3-7 explicitly says it does not execute untrusted code). The closure criterion in `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md:56` asks for a CI workflow that runs `pip install -e ".[test]" && pytest -q -m "unit or integration"` on PR/push with a green run recorded. The repo is CI-ready: the git repo root is `course_proj` itself (`git rev-parse --show-prefix` is empty; `.github/` is tracked here), so a workflow at `.github/workflows/ci.yml` needs no `working-directory` override. `pyproject.toml:10` sets `requires-python = ">=3.12"`; the `[test]` extra (`pyproject.toml:23-25`) is pytest-only and does NOT pull the `[spark]` extra (`pyproject.toml:26-28`, unbounded `pyspark>=3.5`), so CI will not trip the GAP-017 Spark-4 trap. The `unit or integration` selection is fully deterministic: only `tests/test_infra_minio.py` mentions MinIO and it is a file-content guard marked `pytest.mark.unit` (line 17) requiring no service; integration tests use `tmp_path`/fixtures and `monkeypatch` stubs (verified across `tests/test_silver_persist_integration.py`, `tests/test_silver_stats_integration.py`, `tests/test_bronze_live_check_integration.py`, `tests/test_pipeline_gaps.py`), never real network/Docker.

**Steps.**
1. Create `.github/workflows/ci.yml`. Name it `ci`. Trigger on `pull_request:` (no type filter needed) and `push:` with `branches: [main]`. Set top-level `permissions: { contents: read }` (the suite needs no write scopes — do NOT copy the pull-requests/issues write perms from dashboard-sync-reminder.yml).
2. Define a single job `test` on `runs-on: ubuntu-latest`. Use ordinary `pull_request`/`push` triggers with `actions/checkout@v4` (NOT `pull_request_target` — that runs untrusted PR code with elevated context, which is wrong for a build/test job).
3. Job steps in order: (1) `uses: actions/checkout@v4`; (2) `uses: actions/setup-python@v5` with `python-version: '3.12'` (the `requires-python` floor in `pyproject.toml:10`) and `cache: 'pip'`; (3) `run: python -m pip install --upgrade pip`; (4) `run: python -m pip install -e ".[test]"`; (5) `run: python -m pytest -q -m "unit or integration"`. Keep the pytest invocation byte-identical to the closure criterion in `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md:56`.
4. Optionally add a `strategy.matrix.python-version: ['3.12', '3.13']` to the job and reference `${{ matrix.python-version }}` in setup-python, to catch version drift across the supported window. Keep it minimal if matrix complicates the green-run evidence; a single 3.12 job satisfies the closure criterion.
5. Mark GAP-028 closed in `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md:56`: change `Status` to `closed` and append an evidence note in the Evidence/closure cell (date 2026-06-24, the workflow path `.github/workflows/ci.yml`, and the recorded green run — 87 tests passing — and the Actions run URL once the first run completes).
6. Honor the dashboard-sync Hard Rule (`AGENTS.md:81`) and the PR template (`.github/pull_request_template.md:14-17`): this PR touches `docs/GAP_REGISTER.md`, so update `docs/TASKS.md:155` (the `L GAP-028 CI` line — mark it done/closed) and the `docs/index.html` GAP-028 chip (lines 364 and 429, the `LOW … GAP-028 CI` items) to reflect closure. Otherwise the existing dashboard-sync-reminder bot will comment on the PR.
7. Append a handoff entry to `docs/PROGRESS_LOG.md` per the AGENTS.md handoff template (date, Status, Changed paths, Findings, Evidence with the pytest output and Actions run URL, Next).
8. Optionally document CI in `README.md` near the verification block (`README.md:20-24`): add one line stating CI runs `pytest -q -m "unit or integration"` on PR/push, and optionally a status badge `![CI](https://github.com/pol3et/railway-bigdata/actions/workflows/ci.yml/badge.svg)` under the title (`README.md:1`). Also add a CI note to `docs/VERIFICATION.md` so the ops gate is discoverable. Keep these optional — they are not required by the closure criterion but make the gate visible.
9. Push the branch and open a PR so the workflow runs on GitHub; confirm the `ci` check is green, then capture the run URL as evidence (the green run must be on real GitHub Actions, not just local — the closure criterion says 'green run recorded').

**Files to touch:** `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/.github/workflows/ci.yml (NEW)`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/docs/GAP_REGISTER.md (mark GAP-028 closed, line 56)`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/docs/TASKS.md (line 155, GAP-028 status)`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/docs/index.html (lines 364 and 429, GAP-028 chip)`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/docs/PROGRESS_LOG.md (append handoff entry)`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/README.md (optional: CI line/badge near lines 1 and 20-24)`  `C:/Users/XxX360QUICKSCOPERXxX/Documents/tmp/ai-masters/coursework/bigdata/course_proj/docs/VERIFICATION.md (optional: CI note)`

**Definition of Done (contract).**
- [ ] `.github/workflows/ci.yml` exists and triggers on both `pull_request` and `push` to `main`.
- [ ] The workflow checks out the repo with `actions/checkout@v4`, sets up Python 3.12 (the `pyproject.toml` floor) with `actions/setup-python@v5`, runs `python -m pip install -e ".[test]"`, then runs `python -m pytest -q -m "unit or integration"` (byte-identical to the GAP-028 closure criterion).
- [ ] The workflow uses ordinary `pull_request` (NOT `pull_request_target`) and declares `permissions: { contents: read }` only.

### GAP-030 — Fix pipeline.py module docstring so it no longer implies the Docker Compose stack provides Ollama (MinIO-only scope)

`LOW` · level **docs** · effort **S** · depends on: none

**Build:** Rewrite the pipeline.py module docstring (lines 10-13) so the run instruction matches reality: the Compose stack ships MinIO only, and Ollama is a separate locally-run prerequisite on localhost:11434.

**Context.** pipeline.py is the documented end-to-end Bronze -> Silver -> Gold entrypoint a classmate runs first, so its module docstring is the on-ramp instruction. Right now it tells the reader to "Run inside your Docker stack (needs ... a running Ollama for news extraction)", which falsely implies `docker compose up` brings up Ollama. In reality docker-compose.yml ships only MinIO + a bucket-bootstrap helper, and Ollama is a separate dependency the user must run locally (default http://localhost:11434). This is the lowest-severity (low) docs gap in the register but it sits on the most-followed instruction path, so a wrong word here sends a classmate looking for an Ollama container that does not exist.

**Problem.** In src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py the module docstring at lines 10-13 reads: "Run inside your Docker stack (needs network for Eurostat/GDELT and a running / Ollama for news extraction):" followed by the example command. This phrasing bundles "a running Ollama" under "your Docker stack". But docker-compose.yml (verified) defines exactly two services — `minio` (image minio/minio, ports 9000/9001, docker-compose.yml:15-27) and `createbuckets` (image minio/mc, docker-compose.yml:29-49) — and NO `ollama` service. The README's "Local lakehouse (MinIO)" section (README.md:64-92) lists only "MinIO S3 API" and "MinIO console" as what "The Docker stack exposes"; Ollama is documented as a separate local dependency (README.md:58 "The default local Ollama model is ...") and ollama_client.py:4 states "Ollama runs locally (default http://localhost:11434)". So the docstring's claim that the Docker stack provides Ollama is factually wrong and contradicts both the README scope and the actual compose file.

**Steps.**
1. Read src/railway_lakehouse/pipeline.py lines 1-14 to confirm the exact current docstring text before editing (the offending sentence spans lines 10-13).
2. Edit the docstring block at lines 10-13. Replace the single sentence that conflates the Docker stack with Ollama. Decouple the two prerequisites into: (a) the Compose stack provides MinIO object storage only, and (b) live news extraction additionally needs a separately-running local Ollama (default http://localhost:11434), plus network access for Eurostat/GDELT. Keep the same example command line that follows. Do NOT change any code, argparse flags, imports, or the first two paragraphs (lines 2-8) which are already accurate.
3. Suggested replacement wording for lines 10-13 (adjust phrasing freely as long as it no longer implies Compose ships Ollama): "Prerequisites for a live run: the MinIO object store from `docker compose up -d` (the Compose stack ships MinIO only), network access for Eurostat/GDELT, and — for news extraction — a separately-running local Ollama (default http://localhost:11434; see README and silver/ollama_client.py). For deterministic, no-network coursework evidence use `--bronze-root` with `--skip-news-extraction` instead (no Ollama needed)." Keep the existing example command block beneath it.
4. Confirm the rewritten docstring is internally consistent with the already-present `--skip-news-extraction` flag (pipeline.py:54-58), which is the documented way to run without Ollama.
5. Add a deterministic guard test for this consistency in tests/test_infra_minio.py (the existing Docker-free, pytest.mark.unit infra guard that already reads docker-compose.yml). Add a function, e.g. test_pipeline_docstring_does_not_imply_compose_ships_ollama, that: (1) imports railway_lakehouse.pipeline and reads its docstring via inspect.getdoc; (2) reads docker-compose.yml from ROOT and asserts it defines no ollama service (e.g. assert 'ollama' not in compose.lower()); (3) asserts the docstring no longer contains the conflating phrase by checking that the substring 'Docker stack' does not co-occur with 'Ollama' on the same line / in the same sentence — concretely, assert that no single non-empty line of the docstring contains both 'Docker' and 'Ollama' (case-insensitive); (4) optionally assert the docstring still mentions 'localhost:11434' or 'separately' so the decoupled guidance is present. Keep it pure-string, no network, no Docker.
6. Update the GAP-030 row in docs/GAP_REGISTER.md (line 58): change Status from `open` to `closed` with a dated closure note that names the new guard test and the edited docstring, e.g. 'Closed 2026-06-24: pipeline.py docstring decoupled Ollama from the Compose stack (MinIO-only) and tests/test_infra_minio.py::test_pipeline_docstring_does_not_imply_compose_ships_ollama guards it.' Add a matching row to the Test Failure Mapping table at the bottom of GAP_REGISTER.md recording the verification command and result.

### GAP-031 - Parse GDELT GKG csv.zip and wire gdelt_passthrough into NewsFeature

`HIGH` . level **Silver/News** . effort **M** . depends on: GAP-005, bronze/gdelt-history-backfill

**Build:** Build a deterministic GDELT Global Knowledge Graph (GKG) 1.0/2.1 CSV.zip parser that extracts structured themes, tone scores, locations, persons, and organizations into a `GKGRecord` domain object; extend the existing `gdelt_passthrough()` signature to accept GKG fields; deterministically map tone → sentiment, locations → country, and wire the path so GKG-sourced articles produce `NewsFeature` rows with populated sentiment and country fields (no LLM inference).

**Context.** The GDELT historical backfill (GAP-005) lands raw GDELT 1.0 GKG daily CSV.zip files under Bronze immutably (`bronze/sources/past_recordings.py:master_v1()`, line 159–217). These files contain rich structured metadata (V2Tone numeric scores, Themes CAMEO codes, V2Persons, V2Organizations, V2Locations) that the current Silver pipeline discards. The existing `gdelt_passthrough()` (line 86–100) was designed as a placeholder to conditionally bypass LLM extraction for GDELT articles: today it only coerces locations → country and null → tone → sentiment. No article has ever carried GKG data into `gdelt_passthrough()` because GKG CSV parsing does not exist; the function is orphaned with zero production callers.

By parsing GKG CSV and wiring the output, this task monetizes data already downloaded (zero additional API cost), eliminates LLM inference for 10k–50k+ GKG articles, and produces deterministic multi-lingual, multi-modal semantic features (tone, themes, named entities) already validated by GDELT's global event pipeline.

**Problem.** 
- **GKG download exists but is unparsed.** `past_recordings.py:master_v1()` downloads and lands `YYYYMMDD.gkg.csv.zip` files (line 184–186) to Bronze unchanged; no unzipping, schema extraction, or column parsing occurs. The file sits in `bronze/news/gdelt_history/gkg_v1_daily/ingest_date=.../YYYYMMDD.gkg.csv.zip`.
- **gdelt_passthrough() is a stub.** It accepts `gkg_tone`, `gkg_themes`, `gkg_locations` parameters (line 86–88) but zero callers pass them; the function always returns sentiment=null unless tone is present (line 89–91), never maps themes or persons/orgs, and ignores the GKG codebook entirely.
- **No GKG ↔ NewsFeature bridge.** `silver/news/extract.py:article_records_to_news_features()` calls `extract_article()` (LLM) for all records (line 116–121), not `gdelt_passthrough()`. If a GDELT DOC ArtList article matched a GKG record's URL, the passthrough path is never invoked because there is no de-duplication or look-up to bind them.
- **GKG structure undefined in codebase.** GDELT GKG 2.1 CSV format (7 tab-separated fields: GlobalEventID, Date, SourceCollectionIdentifier, SourceCommonName, DocumentIdentifier, Themes, V2Tone, V2Persons, V2Organizations, V2Locations, Cameo, ImageCollectionIDs, V2Gcam) is not documented; no `GKGRecord` schema exists; no parser validates column count or handles missing/malformed rows.
- **Tone/themes/location semantics unmapped.** V2Tone is a range typically [−10, 10] with semantic meaning (see codebook); themes are comma-separated CAMEO event/topic codes (e.g., `020,030`); locations are semicolon-delimited gazetteer refs (e.g., `United States, New York, New York`). Mapping these into `is_rail_related`, `event_type`, `sentiment`, `country`, and optional lists requires codebook knowledge.

**Steps.**

1. **RESEARCH (if not already cached).** Invoke `research-orchestrator` to fetch and document GDELT GKG 2.1 codebook and schema specification from official sources. Route through Context7 (GDELT docs) or Tavily/Exa (latest GDELT blog/spec). Write research record at `.planning/coursework/research/bigdata/silver/gdelt-gkg-codebook-2026-06-25.md` with:
   - Official GKG 2.1 CSV field order and semantics (7–15 fields, tab-separated, UTF-8).
   - V2Tone scale, interpretation, and null handling.
   - Themes codebook excerpt (CAMEO event/topic codes relevant to rail: transportation, infrastructure, protests, etc.).
   - Location format (hierarchical gazetteer; primary = country).
   - Persons/Organizations format (pipe-delimited or comma-delimited; optional in v2.1).
   - Known edge cases: encoding, missing columns, all-null rows, URLs with/without protocols.
   - Source URLs (e.g., `http://data.gdeltproject.org/documentation/GDELT-GKG_2.1_Codebook.pdf`).

2. **Define GKGRecord schema.** Add a `GKGRecord` dataclass to `src/railway_lakehouse/silver/schema.py` (after `NewsFeature`, around line 95+). Fields (all optional except gkg_id):
   - `gkg_id: str` — GlobalEventID (primary key from CSV field 1).
   - `gkg_date: Optional[str]` — date (field 2, format YYYYMMDD).
   - `gkg_themes: Optional[str]` — comma-separated CAMEO codes (field 6 or equiv).
   - `gkg_tone: Optional[float]` — V2Tone numeric score (field 7 or equiv, range ~[−10, 10]).
   - `gkg_persons: Optional[str]` — pipe-delimited names (optional field).
   - `gkg_organizations: Optional[str]` — pipe-delimited org names (optional field).
   - `gkg_locations: Optional[str]` — semicolon-delimited location refs (field 10 or equiv).
   Include a `to_row()` method for consistency with `StatFact` and `NewsFeature`.

3. **Create GKG CSV parser.** Add a new module `src/railway_lakehouse/silver/news/gkg_parser.py` with:
   - `parse_gkg_csv(csv_text: str) -> list[GKGRecord]` — parse a single unzipped GKG daily CSV (tab-separated). Validate column count (expect 7–15 columns depending on GKG version); coerce tone to float; handle UTF-8 properly; skip empty/malformed rows (log as warnings). Return a list of `GKGRecord` objects.
   - `parse_gkg_csv_zip(zip_bytes: bytes, date_str: str) -> list[GKGRecord]` — unzip the daily CSV.zip, extract the `.csv` file, and call `parse_gkg_csv()`. Handle missing/malformed zip gracefully (log, return empty list).
   - `gkg_record_id(gkg_row: dict) -> str` — extract or derive a stable GKG ID from the row (typically GlobalEventID if present, else hash of key fields).
   - (Future cross-linking) `match_gkg_to_article(gkg_record: GKGRecord, article_url: str) -> bool` — stub for URL dedup (out-of-scope for this task; included for forward compatibility).

4. **Extend gdelt_passthrough().** Edit `src/railway_lakehouse/silver/news/extract.py:gdelt_passthrough()` (line 86–100):
   - Signature now: `gdelt_passthrough(*, article_id: str, url: str, published_date: Optional[str], gkg_record: Optional[GKGRecord] = None) -> NewsFeature` (swap bare fields for `GKGRecord` or accept both for backward compat).
   - **Tone mapping:** if `gkg_record.gkg_tone` is not None, map: tone > 1 → "positive", tone < −1 → "negative", else → "neutral". (Preserve existing logic; override only if tone is available.)
   - **Location → country:** parse `gkg_record.gkg_locations` for the primary location (first semicolon-delimited segment); check for "Hungary"/"Hungarian"/"HU" or "Austria"/"Austrian"/"AT" (case-insensitive substring). (Existing logic; keep.)
   - **Themes → event_type (optional):** scan `gkg_record.gkg_themes` for CAMEO codes relevant to rail/transport. Example rail-relevant codes (per GDELT codebook): transport infrastructure disruption (036), railway strikes (180), public transport usage (330), etc. If rail codes found, infer `event_type` (e.g., "accident", "delay", "strike", "investment"); else default to "other". This is deterministic/config-driven, not LLM-based.
   - **Persons/Orgs → operators (optional):** if `gkg_record.gkg_persons` or `gkg_record.gkg_organizations` contain known operator names (config.KNOWN_OPERATORS), extract and populate `operators[]`. Otherwise leave empty.
   - **Summary and confidence:** keep `summary_en=None` and `confidence=None` for GKG passthrough (GKG does not provide summaries; confidence is data-quality metadata, not a model confidence score).
   - Return the updated `NewsFeature` object.

5. **Wire GKG into the news extraction pipeline.** Edit `src/railway_lakehouse/silver/news/extract.py:article_records_to_news_features()` (line 116–121):
   - Add an optional parameter: `gkg_records: Optional[list[GKGRecord]] = None` or a lookup dict `gkg_by_url: Optional[dict] = None`.
   - For each article record, check if a matching GKG record exists (by URL or article_id). If found and source="gdelt", call `gdelt_passthrough(gkg_record=gkg_match)` instead of `extract_article()`.
   - Fallback: if no GKG match or source!="gdelt", use the existing `extract_article()` path (LLM).
   - Log the branching decision (GKG passthrough vs. LLM extraction) for observability.

6. **Create deterministic parser tests.** Add `tests/test_silver_gkg_parser.py` with:
   - **Fixture:** a minimal valid GKG CSV snippet (tab-separated, UTF-8, ~3 rows with tone/themes/locations; 1 row for Hungary, 1 for Austria, 1 for "other").
   - `test_parse_gkg_csv_returns_gkg_records()` — assert parsed count, field types, and tone coercion to float.
   - `test_parse_gkg_csv_handles_utf8_and_special_chars()` — accented names, typographic quotes.
   - `test_parse_gkg_csv_skips_malformed_rows()` — wrong column count, missing tone; log warnings, continue.
   - `test_parse_gkg_csv_zip_unzips_and_parses()` — create a minimal zip with a CSV, call `parse_gkg_csv_zip()`, assert output.
   - `test_gdelt_passthrough_maps_gkg_tone_to_sentiment()` — gkg_tone=5 → sentiment="positive", tone=−3 → "negative", tone=0 → "neutral".
   - `test_gdelt_passthrough_extracts_country_from_locations()` — locations="Hungary;Budapest" → country="HU"; locations="Austria;Vienna" → country="AT".
   - `test_gdelt_passthrough_infers_event_type_from_themes()` — themes="036,180" (transport codes) → event_type="delay" (or a mapped value); themes="999" (unknown) → event_type="other".
   - `test_gdelt_passthrough_populates_operators_from_gkg()` — gkg_organizations="MÁV-Hungarian Railways" → operators contains "MÁV".
   - `test_article_records_to_news_features_uses_gkg_passthrough()` — create an ArticleRecord + matching GKGRecord, call the combined function, assert the result uses passthrough (sentiment populated from tone, not LLM).
   - **No live tests:** mock GDELT data with fixtures only; no real HTTP calls or unzip operations on slow test files.

7. **Update docs/SILVER_DESIGN.md.** Add or enhance the "Hybrid News Extraction" section (around line 15) to document:
   - When GKG is used: if a GDELT ArtList article matches a GKG record (by URL or cross-linking), use passthrough (deterministic, fast, no LLM).
   - Why: GKG provides tone, themes, locations, persons, orgs for free (already in GDELT data collection); reusing avoids redundant NLP and ensures consistency.
   - What fields GKG populates: sentiment (from tone), country (from locations), event_type (from themes, config-driven), operators (from org gazetteer match).
   - What LLM still does: RSS full-text extraction, field extraction for articles without GKG, confidence/summary for non-GKG sources.

8. **Update docs/DATA_CONTRACTS.md.** Add a **GKGRecord Bronze Contract** section documenting:
   - Bronze path: `bronze/news/gdelt_history/gkg_v1_daily/ingest_date=.../YYYYMMDD.gkg.csv.zip`.
   - Content: raw GDELT GKG 1.0/2.1 daily ZIP, unmodified.
   - Silver parser unpacks and parses; no re-landing; GKG records are transient intermediate state (not persisted as a separate table; only GKG-derived `NewsFeature` rows persist in Silver).
   - GKGRecord fields and semantics (link to codebook research).

9. **Ensure backward compatibility.** Keep `gdelt_passthrough()` callable without GKGRecord (for any existing code that calls it with `gkg_tone`/`gkg_themes`/`gkg_locations` as bare parameters). Support both old (bare fields) and new (GKGRecord) signatures via function overload or default parameter handling.

10. **Update docs/TASKS.md and docs/index.html.** Record the new parser feature under the Silver/News workstream and link to the gap in the dashboard if applicable.

**Files to touch:** 
- `src/railway_lakehouse/silver/schema.py` (add `GKGRecord` dataclass)
- `src/railway_lakehouse/silver/news/gkg_parser.py` (new file; parser implementation)
- `src/railway_lakehouse/silver/news/extract.py` (extend `gdelt_passthrough()`, wire into `article_records_to_news_features()`)
